<chapter>
<metadata.block><metadata field="right.running.head"><value>Cooperatives</value></metadata></metadata.block>
<front>
<outline.name.block><label>Chapter</label><designator>32</designator><name>Cooperatives</name></outline.name.block>
<scope.statement.block>
<para><para.text>This chapter contains forms of and relating to the organization of cooperative associations, as well as forms of marketing agreements for use by agricultural cooperatives. The chapter also contains a discussion of legal principles, including tax aspects, that should be considered when drafting these organizing instruments and marketing agreements.</para.text></para>
</scope.statement.block>

<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>32:1</designator><name>Definitions</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Associations" numref="101 et seq." numrange="y">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Associations &key;101 et seq.</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|1|32:1"><para.text>A &ldquo;cooperative corporation&rdquo; is an organization created by the banding together of persons for their common advantage or advancement, financial or otherwise, and is organized for the mutual benefit of its members, without gain to itself.<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|1|32:1"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="13">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;13</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alrfed1" titlename="Monopolies: construction of sec. 1 of the Capper-Volstead Act (7 U.S.C.A. sec. 291) authorizing persons engaged in the production of agricultural products to act together in association" volref="20" pageref="924">Monopolies: construction of sec. 1 of the Capper-Volstead Act (7 U.S.C.A. sec. 291) authorizing persons engaged in the production of agricultural products to act together in association, 20 A.L.R. Fed. 924</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Cooperative corporations, generally, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="59, 60" secrange="y">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &dblsect;59, 60</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Definition and nature of cooperative associations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="aj2" topicname="Cooperative Associations" secref="1">Am. Jur. 2d, Cooperative Associations &sect;1</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> The most common type of cooperative corporation is the nonprofit agricultural cooperative corporation and the New York statutes expressly provide for the organization of such corporations.<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|1|32:1"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="110 et seq." secrange="y">Coop. Corp. Law &dblsect;110 et seq.</cite></para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Agricultural cooperative corporations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="30">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;30</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|1|32:1"><para.text>Cooperative corporations are distinguished from other business structures by the features of democratic control and voting, the distribution of economic benefits on an equal basis or in proportion to the use made of the corporation facilities, limited return on capital, and the fact that most of the cooperative&apos;s business is done with its own members.<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|1|32:1"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="14">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;14</cite> for a list of the general powers of a cooperative corporation.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Agricultural cooperative corporations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="30">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;30</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Distinctive features of cooperative associations. <cite type="secondary" normalpub="aj2" topicname="Cooperative Associations" secref="2">Am. Jur. 2d, Cooperative Associations &sect;2</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> It should be noted that federal legislation authorizing associations of agricultural producers applies only to corporations that, inter alia, allow only one vote per member, or that do not pay dividends on stock or membership capital in excess of 12&percnt; per year. The New York statute establishes these criteria.<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|1|32:1"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="44">Coop. Corp. Law &dblsect;44</cite>, <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="111">111</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Agricultural cooperative corporations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="30">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;30</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Voting by members of cooperative associations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="916">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;916</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
</section.body>

<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>32:2</designator><name>General background</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Agriculture" numref="6">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Agriculture &key;6</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Associations" numref="101 et seq." numrange="y">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Associations &key;101 et seq.</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|2|32:2"><para.text>Agricultural cooperative corporations are governed by the provisions of the New York Cooperative Corporations Law, specifically Sections 110 to 113. Under these statutes, any five or more producers of agricultural products may form a nonprofit, cooperative agricultural corporation, with or without stock, by subscribing and filing a certificate of incorporation.<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|2|32:2"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="112">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;112</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Specific requirements pertaining to cooperative corporations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="73">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;73</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Purposes of agricultural cooperative corporations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="61, 62" secrange="y">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &dblsect;61, 62</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|2|32:2"><para.text>The New York Business Corporation Law also applies in areas that are not directly addressed by the Cooperative Corporations Law, with certain exceptions that are delineated in <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="5">Section 5 of the Cooperative Corporations Law</cite>. Organizations operating under this type of statutory provision are generally exempt from prosecution for certain actions that might otherwise be considered as being in restraint of trade.<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Application of business corporation law to cooperative corporations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="5">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;5</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Agricultural cooperatives and antitrust laws, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="aj2" topicname="Monopolies, Restraints of Trade, and Unfair Trade Practices" secref="225 to 229" secrange="y">Am. Jur. 2d, Monopolies, Restraints of Trade, and Unfair Trade Practices &dblsect;225 to 229</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|2|32:2"><para.text>Cooperative corporations are deemed to be nonprofit corporations, inasmuch as their primary objective is not to make profits or to pay dividends on invested capital, but to provide service, whereby the members may have the economic advantage of cooperative action, which includes a reasonable return for their product and service.<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|2|32:2"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="3" subref="(d)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;3(d)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|2|32:2"><para.text>Cooperative corporations are generally organized to secure for their members the advantages of cooperative bargaining in selling their products, marketing such products, and turning back to the members or other producers the proceeds of sales, less the necessary marketing expenses.<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|2|32:2"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="13">Coop. Corp. Law &dblsect;13</cite> and <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="110">110</cite> for a comprehensive statement of the purposes for organizing a cooperative corporation.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alrfed1" titlename="Construction and application of provision in Robinson-Patman Act (15 USC sec. 13c) exempting nonprofit institutions from price discrimination provision of the Act" volref="3" pageref="996">Construction and application of provision in Robinson-Patman Act (15 USC sec. 13c) exempting nonprofit institutions from price discrimination provision of the Act, 3 A.L.R. Fed. 996</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>For a discussion of cooperative corporations, generally, see <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="59">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;59</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Purposes of cooperative associations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="aj2" topicname="Cooperative Associations" secref="4">Am. Jur. 2d, Cooperative Associations &sect;4</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|2|32:2"><para.text>Other types of cooperatives authorized by statute in New York, but not treated to any extent in this article, are worker cooperative corporations,<footnote><footnote.reference>5</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|2|32:2"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="80 to 94" secrange="y">Coop. Corp. Law &dblsect;80 to 94</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Worker cooperative corporations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="33">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;33</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> cooperative credit corporations,<footnote><footnote.reference>6</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|2|32:2"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="120 to 123" secrange="y">Coop. Corp. Law &dblsect;120 to 123</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Agency and credit cooperative corporations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="31">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;31</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> and cooperatives for the purpose of providing electrical power to rural areas.<footnote><footnote.reference>7</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|2|32:2"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-ruraleleccoop" secref="1 to 72" secrange="y">Rural Elec. Coop. Law &dblsect;1 to 72</cite>; <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="76">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;76</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Rural electric cooperatives, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="32">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;32</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|2|32:2"><para.text>Cooperative corporations organized under the laws of other states or any foreign corporation that has as its purpose or among its purposes the cooperative rendering of mutual support to its members may, in furtherance of its cooperative objectives, do business in New York and make and enforce contracts in the state upon compliance with the provisions of the New York Cooperative Corporations Law and with other laws applicable to foreign corporations.<footnote><footnote.reference>8</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|2|32:2"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="76">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;76</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Foreign cooperative corporations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="64">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;64</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|2|32:2"><para.text>In addition to the powers specified in the Cooperative Corporations Law, cooperative corporations possess the powers and rights set out in the Business Corporation Law and the N.Y. Not-for-Profit Corporation Law subject to the provisions of the Cooperative Corporations Law.<footnote><footnote.reference>9</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|2|32:2"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="14">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;14</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Powers of cooperative corporations, generally, see <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="472 to 476" secrange="y">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &dblsect;472 to 476</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
</section.body>

<outline.name.block>
<designator>1</designator><name>Federal Tax</name></outline.name.block>

<analytical.level.body>
<section.block>
<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>32:3</designator><name>In general</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Internal Revenue" numref="3985 to 3988" numrange="y">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Internal Revenue &key;3985 to 3988</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Internal Revenue" numref="4059">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Internal Revenue &key;4059</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|3|32:3"><para.text>For federal income tax purposes, cooperatives are classified either as exempt farmers&apos; cooperatives or nonexempt cooperatives. An &ldquo;exempt farmers&apos; cooperative&rdquo; is an association of farmers, fruit growers, or the like, organized and operated on a cooperative basis for the purpose of marketing the products of members or other producers and turning back to them the proceeds of sales, less the necessary marketing expenses, on the basis of either the quantity or the value of the products furnished by them; or purchasing supplies and equipment for the use of members or other persons and turning over such supplies and equipment to them at actual cost plus necessary expenses.<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|3|32:3"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="521" subref="(b)" pararef="(1)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;521(b)(1)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Agricultural and horticultural organizations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-4700 to D-4705" parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d &dblpara;D-4700 to D-4705</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Cooperatives, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="E-1000 to E-1150" parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d &dblpara;E-1000 to E-1150</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Farmers&apos; cooperatives, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="5:17 to 5:20" secrange="y">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &dblsect;5:17 to 5:20</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|3|32:3"><para.text>A &ldquo;nonexempt cooperative&rdquo; can be defined as one that does not meet the requirements of an exempt farmers&apos; cooperative either because it engages in occupations dissimilar to those of farmers, fruit growers, and the like<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|3|32:3"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.521-1" subref="(d)">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.521-1(d)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>What cooperative exemption means, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="E-1002">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d &para;E-1002</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Nonexempt farmers cooperatives, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="5:17 to 5:19" secrange="y">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &dblsect;5:17 to 5:19</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> or because it fails to satisfy some other requirement.<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|3|32:3"><para.text>See, generally, <cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.521-1">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.521-1</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> Most other cooperative corporations are generally taxable as ordinary business corporations, except that they may exclude from their income earnings distributed as patronage dividends.<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|3|32:3"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1381" subref="(a)">26 U.S.C.A. &dblsect;1381(a)</cite>, <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1382" subref="(b)">1382(b)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>For general discussion of taxation of cooperatives, see <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="5:17 to 5:20" secrange="y">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &dblsect;5:17 to 5:20</cite> and <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="E-1000 to E-1045" parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d &dblpara;E-1000 to E-1045</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> This chapter is concerned primarily with exempt farmers&apos; cooperatives.</para.text></para>
</section.body>
</section>
<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>32:4</designator><name>Tax consequences for exempt farmers&apos; cooperative</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Internal Revenue" numref="3985 to 3988" numrange="y">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Internal Revenue &key;3985 to 3988</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|4|32:4"><para.text>An &ldquo;exempt farmers&apos; cooperative&rdquo; is subject to the general corporation income tax and the alternative tax on capital gains.<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|4|32:4"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1381" subref="(b)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1381(b)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|4|32:4"><para.text>For the general corporation income tax, see <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="11">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;11</cite>; for alternative tax on capital gains, see <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1201">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1201</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>How cooperatives are taxed, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="E-1001">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d&para;E-1001</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Taxation of farmers&apos; cooperatives, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="5:17">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;5:17</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> However, in determining taxable income, such organizations need not take into account amounts paid during the payment period for the taxable year: as certain patronage dividends;<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|4|32:4"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1382" subref="(b)" pararef="(1)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1382(b)(1)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alr3" titlename="Co-operative associations: rights in equity credits or patronage dividends" volref="50" pageref="435">Co-operative associations: rights in equity credits or patronage dividends, 50 A.L.R.3d 435</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Co-op&apos;s deduction of patronage dividends, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="E-1101">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d &para;E-1101</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Noncash patronage dividends, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="5:18">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;5:18</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> in money or other property (except written notices of allocation) in redemption of certain nonqualified written notices of allocation;<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|4|32:4"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1382" subref="(b)" pararef="(2)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1382(b)(2)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|4|32:4"><para.text>For a definition of &ldquo;written notice of allocation&rdquo; and discussion of qualified and unqualified notices, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="32:6">&sect;32:6</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> as certain per-unit retain allocations;<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|4|32:4"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1382" subref="(b)" pararef="(3)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1382(b)(3)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Co-op&apos;s deduction of per-unit retain allocations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="E-1101">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d &para;E-1101</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> or in money or other property (except per-unit retain certificates) in redemption of certain nonqualified per-unit retain certificates.<footnote><footnote.reference>5</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|4|32:4"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1382" subref="(b)" pararef="(4)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1382(b)(4)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|4|32:4"><para.text>The &ldquo;patronage dividend&rdquo; is an amount paid to a patron by a Section 1381 organization on the basis of quantity or value of business done with or for such patron; under an obligation of such organization to pay such amount, which obligation existed before the organization received the amount so paid; and that is determined by reference to the net earnings of the organization from business done with or for its patrons.<footnote><footnote.reference>6</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|4|32:4"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1388" subref="(a)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1388(a)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>What is patronage dividend, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="E-1104">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d &para;E-1104</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Noncash patronage dividends, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="5:18">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;5:18</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> The payment period for any taxable year is the period beginning with the first day of such taxable year and ending with the fifteenth day of the ninth month following the close of such year.<footnote><footnote.reference>7</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|4|32:4"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1382" subref="(d)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1382(d)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> &ldquo;Per-unit retain allocation&rdquo; means any allocation, by an exempt cooperative, to a patron with respect to products marketed for such patron, the amount of which is fixed without reference to the net earnings of the organization pursuant to an agreement between the organization and the patron.<footnote><footnote.reference>8</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|4|32:4"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1388" subref="(f)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1388(f)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>&ldquo;Per-unit retain allocation&rdquo; defined, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="E-1126">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d &para;E-1126</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> &ldquo;Per-unit retain certificate&rdquo; means any written notice that discloses to the recipient the stated dollar amount of a per-unit retain allocation to such recipient by the organization.<footnote><footnote.reference>9</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|4|32:4"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1388" subref="(g)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1388(g)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> A &ldquo;qualified per-unit retain certificate&rdquo; is any per-unit retain certificate that the distributee has agreed, in a specified manner, to take into account at its stated dollar amount as provided in <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-irc" titleref="26" secref="1385" subref="(a)">Section 1385(a) of the Internal Revenue Code</cite>.<footnote><footnote.reference>10</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|4|32:4"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1388" subref="(h)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1388(h)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> &ldquo;Nonqualified per-unit retain certificate&rdquo; means a per-unit retain certificate that does not meet the requirements of a qualified per-unit retain certificate.<footnote><footnote.reference>11</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|4|32:4"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1388" subref="(i)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1388(i)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|4|32:4"><para.text>In addition, the organization may deduct amounts paid during the taxable year as dividends on its capital stock,<footnote><footnote.reference>12</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|4|32:4"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1382" subref="(c)" pararef="(1)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1382(c)(1)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Co-op&apos;s deduction of patronage dividends, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="E-1101">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d &para;E-1101</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Noncash patronage dividends, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="5:18">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;5:18</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> as well as amounts paid during the payment period for the taxable year in money, qualified written notices of allocation, or other property (except nonqualified written notices of allocation) on a patronage basis to patrons with respect to the organization&apos;s earnings during such taxable year that were derived from business done for the United States or any of its agencies or from sources other than patronage.<footnote><footnote.reference>13</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|4|32:4"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1382" subref="(c)" pararef="(2)" spararef="(A)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1382(c)(2)(A)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> It may also deduct amounts paid during the payment period for the taxable year in money or other property (except written notices of allocation) in redemption of a nonqualified written notice of allocation which was paid, during the payment period for the taxable year during which the earnings were derived, on a patronage basis to a patron with respect to earnings derived from business done for the United States or for any of its agencies or from sources other than patronage.<footnote><footnote.reference>14</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|4|32:4"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1382" subref="(c)" pararef="(2)" spararef="(B)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1382(c)(2)(B)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|4|32:4"><para.text>The amount of any patronage dividend that is paid in money, a qualified written notice of allocation, or other property (except a nonqualified written notice of allocation) and that is received by the patron during the taxable year from an exempt farmer&apos;s cooperative must be included in gross income.<footnote><footnote.reference>15</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|4|32:4"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1385" subref="(a)" pararef="(1)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1385(a)(1)</cite>; <cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.1385-1" subref="(a)">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.1385-1(a)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> However, such amount, to the extent that it is properly taken into account as an adjustment to basis of property or is attributable to personal, living, or family items is not includable.<footnote><footnote.reference>16</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|4|32:4"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1385" subref="(b)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1385(b)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> In addition, includable in the patron&apos;s gross income are nonpatronage distributions by tax-exempt farmers&apos; cooperatives paid in money, qualified written notices of allocation, or other property except nonqualified written notices of allocation, received by the patron during the taxable year from such a cooperative,<footnote><footnote.reference>17</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|4|32:4"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1385" subref="(a)" pararef="(2)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1385(a)(2)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> and the amount of any per-unit retain allocation which is paid in qualified per-unit retain certificates and received by the patron during the taxable year from a tax-exempt farmers&apos; cooperative or other specified cooperative.<footnote><footnote.reference>18</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|4|32:4"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1385" subref="(a)" pararef="(3)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1385(a)(3)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|4|32:4"><para.text>An organization claiming exemption must file IRS Form 1028 with the district director for the internal revenue district in which the organization&apos;s principal place of business or principal office is located.<footnote><footnote.reference>19</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|4|32:4"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.521-1" subref="(e)">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.521-1(e)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Applying for exemption, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="E-1043">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d &para;E-1043</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Exempt farmers&apos; cooperatives, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="5:20">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;5:20</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
</section.body>
</section>
<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>32:5</designator><name>Tax consequences for nonexempt cooperative</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Internal Revenue" numref="3985 to 3988" numrange="y">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Internal Revenue &key;3985 to 3988</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|5|32:5"><para.text>A nonexempt cooperative is treated in the same manner as an exempt farmers&apos; cooperative for computation of taxable income, with the exception that a nonexempt cooperative is not entitled to the deductions allowable under <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-irc" titleref="26" secref="1382" subref="(c)">Section 1382(c) of the Internal Revenue Code</cite>.<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|5|32:5"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1382" subref="(c)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1382(c)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|5|32:5"><para.text>For a discussion of such deductions as they relate to exempt farmers&apos; cooperatives, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="32:4">&sect;32:4</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>How cooperatives are taxed, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="E-1001">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d &para;E-1001</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Farmers&apos; cooperatives, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="5:17 to 5:19" secrange="y">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &dblsect;5:17 to 5:19</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
</section.body>
</section>
<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>32:6</designator><name>Written notices of allocation</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Internal Revenue" numref="3985">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Internal Revenue &key;3985</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Internal Revenue" numref="3987">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Internal Revenue &key;3987</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|6|32:6"><para.text>A &ldquo;written notice of allocation&rdquo; is notice in any capital stock, revolving fund certificate, retain certificate, certificate of indebtedness, letter of advice, or other written notice that discloses to the recipient the stated dollar amount allocated to the individual by the organization and the portion, if any, constituting a patronage dividend.<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|6|32:6"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1388" subref="(b)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1388(b)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alr3" titlename="Co-operative associations: rights in equity credits or patronage dividends" volref="50" pageref="435">Co-operative associations: rights in equity credits or patronage dividends, 50 A.L.R.3d 435</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Qualified written notice of allocation, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="E-1121">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d &para;E-1121</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Noncash patronage dividends, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="5:18">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;5:18</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> Such notices are classified as either qualified or nonqualified.<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|6|32:6"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1388" subref="(c), (d)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1388(c), (d)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|6|32:6"><para.text>The &ldquo;qualified written notice of allocation&rdquo; means one that may be redeemed in cash at its stated dollar amount at any time within a period beginning on the date such written notice is paid and ending not earlier than 90 days from such date, but only if the distributee receives written notice of the right of redemption at the time of receipt of the written notice of allocation and a written notice of allocation that the distributee has consented to take into account at its stated dollar amount for purposes of computing the distributee&apos;s gross income.<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|6|32:6"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1388" subref="(c)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1388(c)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> A qualified written notice of allocation does not include a written notice of allocation that is paid as part of the patronage dividend or as part of certain other payments unless 20&percnt; or more of the amount is paid in money or by qualified check.<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|6|32:6"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1388" subref="(c)" pararef="(1)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1388(c)(1)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> A &ldquo;qualified check&rdquo; means only a check (or other instrument that is redeemable in money) that is paid as a part of a patronage dividend or as a part of certain other payments to a distributee who has not consented with respect to such patronage dividend or payment and on which there is clearly imprinted a statement that the endorsement and cashing of the check or other instrument constitutes the payee&apos;s consent to include in his or her gross income, as provided in the federal income tax laws, the stated dollar amount of the written notice of allocation that is part of the patronage dividend or payment of which such qualified check is also a part.<footnote><footnote.reference>5</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|6|32:6"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1388" subref="(c)" pararef="(4)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1388(c)(4)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Patron&apos;s consent by qualified check to report written notice of allocation in income, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="E-1130">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d &para;E-1130</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Noncash patronage dividends, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="5:18">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;5:18</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> A &ldquo;qualified check&rdquo; does not include any check or other instrument that is paid as part of a patronage dividend or payment that does not include a written notice of allocation (other than a written notice of allocation as described in Section 1388(c)(1)(A) of the Code).<footnote><footnote.reference>6</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|6|32:6"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1388" subref="(c)" pararef="(4)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1388(c)(4)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Patron&apos;s consent by qualified check to report written notice of allocation in income, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="E-1130">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d &para;E-1130</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Noncash patronage dividends, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="5:18">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;5:18</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|6|32:6"><para.text>The distributee&apos;s consent may be obtained through the distributee&apos;s written consent;<footnote><footnote.reference>7</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|6|32:6"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1388" subref="(c)" pararef="(2)" spararef="(A)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1388(c)(2)(A)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> the distributee&apos;s obtaining or retaining membership in the cooperative after the organization has adopted a bylaw providing that membership in the organization constitutes such consent and the distributee has received a written notification and copy of such bylaw;<footnote><footnote.reference>8</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|6|32:6"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1388" subref="(c)" pararef="(2)" spararef="(B)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1388(c)(2)(B)</cite> (requiring that such bylaw has been adopted after October 16, 1962).</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|6|32:6"><para.text>For a bylaw provision providing that membership in a cooperative constitutes consent of the member to take allocations into income, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="32:30">&sect;32:30</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Consent of membership, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="E-1129">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d &para;E-1129</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> or the distributee&apos;s endorsement and cashing of a qualified check, paid as part of the patronage dividend or payment of which such written notice of allocation is also a part, on or before the 90th day after the close of the payment period for the taxable year of the organization for which such patronage dividend or payment is paid.<footnote><footnote.reference>9</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|6|32:6"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1388" subref="(c)" pararef="(2)" spararef="(C)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1388(c)(2)(C)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Patron&apos;s consent by qualified check to report written notice of allocation in income, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="E-1130">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d &para;E-1130</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Noncash patronage dividends, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="5:18">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;5:18</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|6|32:6"><para.text>A &ldquo;nonqualified written notice of allocation&rdquo; is a written notice of allocation that is not described as a qualified written notice of allocation or a qualified check that is not cashed on or before the 90th day after the close of the payment period for the taxable year for which the distribution of which it is a part is paid.<footnote><footnote.reference>10</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|6|32:6"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1388" subref="(d)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1388(d)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Nonqualified written notices of allocation, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="E-1122">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d &para;E-1122</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Noncash patronage dividends, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="5:18">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;5:18</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
</section.body>

<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>32:7</designator><name>In general</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Agriculture" numref="6">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Agriculture &key;6</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Taxation" numref="3400 to 3599" numrange="y">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Taxation &key;3400 to 3599</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|7|32:7"><para.text>The New York tax upon and with respect to personal income<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|7|32:7"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-tax" secref="601 et seq." secrange="y">NYTL &dblsect;601 et seq.</cite></para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> imposes a tax on the income of every resident individual of the state.<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|7|32:7"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-tax" secref="601">NYTL &sect;601</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> The term &ldquo;resident individual&rdquo; applies only to natural persons. Partnerships, as such, are not subject to this tax.<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|7|32:7"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-tax" secref="605">NYTL &sect;605</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para><para.text>For discussion of the federal tax provisions relating to agricultural cooperative associations, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="32:3 et seq." secrange="y">&dblsect;32:3 et seq.</cite></para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alr6" titlename="State income tax treatment of partnerships and partners" volref="2" pageref="1">State income tax treatment of partnerships and partners, 2 ALR 6th 1</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>

<outline.name.block>
<designator>II</designator><name>Agricultural Cooperative Corporations</name></outline.name.block>
</front>
<analytical.level.body>
<analytical.level>
<front>
<outline.name.block>
<designator>A</designator><name>Form Drafting Principles</name></outline.name.block>
</front>
<analytical.level.body>
<section.block>
<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>32:8</designator><name>Introduction</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Agriculture" numref="6">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Agriculture &key;6</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|8|32:8"><para.text>A nonprofit cooperative agricultural corporation may be organized to engage in any cooperative activities for its members, including the marketing, selling of, bargaining, and contracting for agricultural products and the by-products of such products.<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|8|32:8"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="110">Coop. Corp. Law &dblsect;110</cite>, <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="112">112</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Agricultural cooperative corporations, generally, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="30">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;30</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Purposes of agricultural cooperative corporations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="61">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;61</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Specific requirements pertaining to cooperative corporations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="73">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;73</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Purposes of cooperative associations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="aj2" topicname="Cooperative Associations" secref="4">Am. Jur. 2d, Cooperative Associations &sect;4</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> Any five or more producers of agricultural products, to include cooperative corporations of such producers organized under the laws of New York or any other state, may form a nonprofit cooperative agricultural corporation, either with or without capital stock.<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|8|32:8"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="111">Coop. Corp. Law &dblsect;111</cite>, <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="112">112</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Specific requirements pertaining to cooperative corporations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="73">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;73</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|8|32:8"><para.text>If the principal activities of the corporation are connected with the marketing, processing, manufacture, or sale of agricultural products, it may be termed a cooperative agricultural corporation and incorporated as such.<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|8|32:8"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="111">Coop. Corp. Law &dblsect;111</cite>, <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="112">112</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> If its principal activities relate to the purchase of supplies for producers of agricultural products, it may be termed a cooperative purchasing association and may be incorporated as such.<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|8|32:8"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="112">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;112</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> In either case, the corporation may engage in both types of activity.<footnote><footnote.reference>5</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|8|32:8"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="112">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;112</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> A nonprofit agricultural cooperative association of this nature may be incorporated with or without capital stock.<footnote><footnote.reference>6</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|8|32:8"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="112">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;112</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|8|32:8"><para.text>The amount of dividends that may be declared on stock cannot exceed 12&percnt; per year.<footnote><footnote.reference>7</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|8|32:8"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="111">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;111</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Agricultural cooperative corporations, generally, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="30">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;30</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|8|32:8"><para.text>The exempt income tax status of farmers&apos; cooperatives is extended even though they have capital stock if the dividend rate of the stock is fixed at a rate not to exceed the legal rate of interest in the state of incorporation or 8&percnt; per year, whichever is greater, on the value of the consideration for which the stock was issued and if substantially all such stock (other than nonvoting preferred stock, the owners of which are not entitled or permitted to participate, directly or indirectly, in the profits of the association, on dissolution or otherwise, beyond the fixed dividends) is owned by producers who market their products or purchase their supplies and equipment through the association.<footnote><footnote.reference>8</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|8|32:8"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="521" subref="(b)" pararef="(2)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;521(b)(2)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Agricultural cooperative corporations, generally, see <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="30">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;30</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|8|32:8"><para.text>Transactions with nonmembers will not bar a farmers&apos; cooperative from claiming an exempt status under the federal income tax laws, provided the value of the transactions, in relation to those with members, does not exceed statutory limits.<footnote><footnote.reference>9</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|8|32:8"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="521" subref="(b)" pararef="(4)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;521(b)(4)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> An exemption will not be denied any association that markets the products of nonmembers in an amount the value of which does not exceed the value of the products marketed for members or which purchases supplies and equipment for nonmembers in an amount the value of which does not exceed the value of the supplies and equipment purchased for members, provided the value of the purchases made for persons who are neither members nor producers does not exceed 15&percnt; of the value of all purchases.<footnote><footnote.reference>10</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|8|32:8"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="521" subref="(b)" pararef="(4)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;521(b)(4)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|8|32:8"><para.text>Business done for the United States or any of its agencies is disregarded in determining the right to exemption.<footnote><footnote.reference>11</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|8|32:8"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="521" subref="(b)" pararef="(5)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;521(b)(5)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|8|32:8"><para.text>The provisions of the Business Corporation Law of New York and all powers and rights conferred under such law apply to agricultural cooperative corporations except where such provisions are in conflict with or are inconsistent with the express provisions of the Agricultural Cooperative Corporations Law.<footnote><footnote.reference>12</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|8|32:8"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="5">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;5</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Application of business corporation law to cooperative corporations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="5 to 7" secrange="y">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &dblsect;5 to 7</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
</section.body>
</section>
<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>32:9</designator><name>Drafting preorganization agreements and certificates of incorporation</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Agriculture" numref="6">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Agriculture &key;6</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|9|32:9"><para.text>In drafting the organization agreement, also commonly known as the preorganization agreement, the general policies of promoting the cultivation and marketing of agricultural products through cooperation and of distributing the agricultural products in as direct a manner as possible between the producer and the consumer should be stated.<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|9|32:9"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="110">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;110</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Agricultural cooperative corporations, generally, see <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="30">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;30</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Specific requirements pertaining to cooperative corporations, see <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="73">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;73</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|9|32:9"><para.text>It is the declared policy of the state of New York to promote the effective production and merchandising of agricultural commodities by providing the means by which farmers may act together in manufacturing, processing, preparing for market, handling and/or marketing their farm products and by enabling farmers to act together in purchasing, testing, grading, processing, distributing and/or furnishing farm supplies and/or farm business services through cooperatives operated for the mutual benefit of the members of the corporations as producers and purchasers.<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|9|32:9"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="110">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;110</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Agricultural cooperative corporations, generally, see <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="30">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;30</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Specific requirements pertaining to cooperative corporations, see <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="73">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;73</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<feature.para.block><name.block><name>Practice Tip:</name></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|9|32:9"><para.text>As eventually drawn, the agreement should bind the producer to belong to and patronize the proposed cooperative and to furnish the specified amount of initial capital, contingent on the signing up of a sufficient number of other prospective members within a given time period. The chief provisions proposed for the bylaws should be indicated and the form of the marketing agreement to be used should be set forth.</para.text></para>
</feature.para.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|9|32:9"><para.text>New York statutory law specifies the matters required to be included in the certificate of incorporation of a cooperative corporation.<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|9|32:9"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="11">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;11</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Specific requirements pertaining to cooperative corporations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="73">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;73</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> These requirements are set out in a subsequent checklist.<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|9|32:9"><para.text>See <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="32:12">&sect;32:12</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> The certificate should specify that the organization will deal only in agricultural products, as defined in <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="110 to 113" secrange="y">Sections 110 to 113 of the New York Cooperative Corporations Law</cite>,<footnote><footnote.reference>5</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|9|32:9"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="3" subref="(a)">Coop. Corp. Law &dblsect;3(a)</cite>, <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="111" subref="(b)">111(b)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> and should make clear that the organization will qualify as an agricultural cooperative within the meaning of the statute.<footnote><footnote.reference>6</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|9|32:9"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="111" subref="(a)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;111(a)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Agricultural cooperative corporations, generally, see <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="30">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;30</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Specific requirements pertaining to cooperative corporations, see <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="73">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;73</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> &ldquo;Agricultural product&rdquo; is defined as any product of cultivating land, and includes floricultural, horticultural, viticultural, forestry, nut, dairy, livestock, poultry, bee, and any farm products or by-products thereof.<footnote><footnote.reference>7</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|9|32:9"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="3" subref="(a)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;3(a)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> An &ldquo;agricultural cooperative&rdquo; is a cooperative, either stock or nonstock, operated for the mutual benefit of the members in which no member is allowed more than one vote because of the amount of stock or membership capital he or she may own therein; the cooperative does not pay dividends on stock or membership capital in excess of 12&percnt; per year; and the cooperative does not deal in farm products, agricultural waste products or agricultural compost, farm supplies, farm business services and the capture of methane and other gases for the generation and use or sale of energy, with or for nonmembers in an amount greater in value than the total amount of such business transacted by it with or for members.<footnote><footnote.reference>8</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|9|32:9"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="111" subref="(a)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;111(a)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|9|32:9"><para.text>Question of whether cooperative is &ldquo;agricultural cooperative corporation&rdquo; within meaning of Agriculture and Markets Law is resolved solely by reference to statutory definition contained in Cooperative Corporations Law. <cite type="case">Atwater v. McGuire, 227 A.D.2d 763, 642 N.Y.S.2d 363 (3d Dep&apos;t 1996)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<feature.para.block><name.block><name>Practice Tips:</name></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|9|32:9"><para.text>Because the certificate of incorporation of an agricultural cooperative association is generally more difficult to amend than its bylaws,<footnote><footnote.reference>9</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|9|32:9"><para.text>For requirements to amend certificates, see <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="12">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;12</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Amendment or repeal of bylaws of cooperative corporations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="128">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;128</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Amending certificate of incorporation of cooperative corporations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="158">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;158</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> it is recommended that the substantive content of the certificate be limited to the statutory requirements.<footnote><footnote.reference>10</footnote.reference><footnote.body>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alr3" titlename="Construction and effect of corporate bylaws or articles relating to change in number of directors" volref="3" pageref="623">Construction and effect of corporate bylaws or articles relating to change in number of directors, 3 A.L.R.3d 623</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
</feature.para.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|9|32:9"><para.text>In general, the provisions of the New York Business Corporation Law applies to agricultural cooperative corporations except where such provisions are in conflict with or are inconsistent with the particular provisions applicable to cooperatives.<footnote><footnote.reference>11</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|9|32:9"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="5">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;5</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|9|32:9"><para.text>For forms and materials appropriate for use under the New York Business Corporation Law, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="17:1 et seq." secrange="y">&dblsect;17:1 et seq.</cite></para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Application of business corporation law to cooperative corporations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="5 to 7" secrange="y">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &dblsect;5 to 7</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
