<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>32:10</designator><name>Drafting certificate of incorporation; formal requirements</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Agriculture" numref="6">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Agriculture &key;6</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|10|32:10"><para.text>The certificate of incorporation must be made, acknowledged, and filed by five or more persons.<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|10|32:10"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="11">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;11</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|10|32:10"><para.text>A corporation&apos;s existence commences upon the filing of a certificate of incorporation with the Department of State. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-buscorp" secref="403">BCL &sect;403</cite>. The certificate is conclusive evidence that all conditions precedent have been fulfilled and that the corporation has been formed under the appropriate statute. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-buscorp" secref="403">BCL &sect;403</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Specific requirements pertaining to cooperative corporations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="73">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;73</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Evidentiary effect of certificate, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="83">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;83</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Commencement of corporate existence, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="109">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;109</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> All the subscribers must be of full age, at least two-thirds of them must be citizens of the United States and at least one of them must be a resident of the State of New York and, of the persons named as directors at least one must be a citizen of the United States and a resident of the State of New York.<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|10|32:10"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="11" subref="(9)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;11(9)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Specific requirements pertaining to cooperative corporations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="73">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;73</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> It may contain any provision, not inconsistent with the law, that the incorporators elect to set forth for the regulation of the internal affairs of the corporation.<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|10|32:10"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-buscorp" secref="402" subref="(c)">BCL &sect;402(c)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> The general requirements for a certificate of incorporation to be filed by a cooperative corporation are set out in the Cooperative Corporations Law.<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|10|32:10"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="11">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;11</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Specific requirements pertaining to cooperative corporations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="73">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;73</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|10|32:10"><para.text>To assist in the processing of documents that are to be filed in the office of the Department of State, the physical appearance and makeup of such documents, including certificates of incorporation, should be in good legal form and be clearly legible.<footnote><footnote.reference>5</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|10|32:10"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-ny-ccr" titleref="19" secref="150.2">19 NYCRR &sect;150.2</cite>; <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-buscorp" secref="104">BCL &sect;104</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<feature.para.block><name.block><name>Practice Tip:</name></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|10|32:10"><para.text>It is recommended that you check with the Secretary of State&apos;s office with regard to the form, filing, and information necessary for the return of the filed certificate.</para.text></para>
</feature.para.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|10|32:10"><para.text>The directors are required periodically to set aside reasonable sums for reserves.<footnote><footnote.reference>6</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|10|32:10"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="72">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;72</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Power of cooperative corporations to establish reserves, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="475">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;475</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> The net margins or net retained proceeds may, in the discretion of the directors, be distributed at least once a year to members or patrons by uniform distribution and calculated on such basis as the bylaws or marketing contract may prescribe.<footnote><footnote.reference>7</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|10|32:10"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="72">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;72</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alr3" titlename="Co-operative associations: rights in equity credits or patronage dividends" volref="50" pageref="435">Co-operative associations: rights in equity credits or patronage dividends, 50 A.L.R.3d 435</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Power of cooperative corporations to establish reserves, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="475">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;475</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> Distributions may be credited on account of the issuance to members or patrons of capital stock or other securities of the corporation.<footnote><footnote.reference>8</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|10|32:10"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="72">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;72</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alr3" titlename="Co-operative associations: rights in equity credits or patronage dividends" volref="50" pageref="435">Co-operative associations: rights in equity credits or patronage dividends, 50 A.L.R.3d 435</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Power of cooperative corporations to establish reserves, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="475">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;475</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> In the case of cooperatives with capital stock, dividends may not exceed 12&percnt; per year on any class of stock.<footnote><footnote.reference>9</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|10|32:10"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="72">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;72</cite>. See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="111">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;111</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alr3" titlename="Co-operative associations: rights in equity credits or patronage dividends" volref="50" pageref="435">Co-operative associations: rights in equity credits or patronage dividends, 50 A.L.R.3d 435</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Power of cooperative corporations to establish reserves, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="475">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;475</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|10|32:10"><para.text>A certificate of incorporation or amendment of such certificate will not take effect until it has been filed with the Secretary of State.<footnote><footnote.reference>10</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|10|32:10"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="15">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;15</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Amending certificate of incorporation of cooperative corporations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="158">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;158</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> The Secretary of State will provide copies of the certificates or amendments to the Commissioner of Agriculture and Markets or his or her designee on request by corporation name.<footnote><footnote.reference>11</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|10|32:10"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="15">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;15</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Additional requirements pertaining to cooperative corporations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="80">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;80</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>

<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>32:11</designator><name>Drafting bylaws</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Agriculture" numref="6">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Agriculture &key;6</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Associations" numref="128">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Associations &key;128</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Associations" numref="129">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Associations &key;129</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|11|32:11"><para.text>The New York Statutes require that bylaws regulating the conduct and manner of the corporation be adopted by its incorporators at the organization meeting.<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|11|32:11"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-buscorp" secref="601" subref="(a)">BCL &sect;601(a)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Power of cooperative corporations to adopt bylaws, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="119">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;119</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> Thereafter, bylaws may be adopted by vote of the holders of the shares at the time entitled to vote in the election of any directors.<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|11|32:11"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-buscorp" secref="601" subref="(a)">BCL &sect;601(a)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> When so provided in the certificate of incorporation or a bylaw adopted by the shareholders, bylaws may also be adopted by the board of directors.<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|11|32:11"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="16">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;16</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alr3" titlename="Co-operative associations: validity and enforceability of by-law amendment reducing benefits available to members" volref="61" pageref="976">Co-operative associations: validity and enforceability of by-law amendment reducing benefits available to members, 61 A.L.R.3d 976</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alr3" titlename="Co-operative associations: rights in equity credits or patronage dividends" volref="50" pageref="435">Co-operative associations: rights in equity credits or patronage dividends, 50 A.L.R.3d 435</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>For a discussion of bylaws, see <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="116 to 129" secrange="y">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &dblsect;116 to 129</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Power of cooperative corporations to establish reserves, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="475">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;475</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|11|32:11"><para.text>Any bylaw adopted by the board of directors must be reported to the annual meeting of the corporation and, if not affirmatively approved at such meeting, will cease to be in effect.<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|11|32:11"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="16">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;16</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> A listing of the matters authorized by statute to be included in the bylaws of an agricultural cooperative association is set out in a subsequent checklist.<footnote><footnote.reference>5</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|11|32:11"><para.text>See <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="32:13">&sect;32:13</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|11|32:11"><para.text>In many respects, the bylaws of an agricultural cooperative resemble those of a business corporation.<footnote><footnote.reference>6</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|11|32:11"><para.text>For forms and discussion relating to corporate bylaws, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="17:1 et seq." secrange="y">&dblsect;17:1 et seq.</cite></para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> However, there are several notable differences. For example, the bylaws of an agricultural marketing cooperative are often tied to a marketing agreement between the cooperative and its members. The bylaws frequently incorporate the agreement by reference and may specify the method to be used to create, accumulate, and maintain the reserves required by statute.<footnote><footnote.reference>7</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|11|32:11"><para.text>See, generally, <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="113">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;113</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Power of cooperative corporations to establish reserves, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="475">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;475</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
</section.body>
</section>
</section.block>
</analytical.level.body>

</research.reference.block>
<item.reference.block>
<item.reference><name.block><label>Item</label><designator>1.</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|12|32:12"><para.text>Where copy of certificate of incorporation was not included in record of shareholders&apos; action contesting their disqualification from voting for board of directors and where corporation&apos;s name did not include word &ldquo;cooperative,&rdquo; it was presumed that corporation was established under Business Corporation Law rather than Cooperative Corporations Law. <cite type="case">Yu v. Linton, 68 A.D.2d 856, 414 N.Y.S.2d 558 (1st Dep&apos;t 1979)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="164 to 179" secrange="y">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &dblsect;164 to 179</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</item.reference>
<item.reference><name.block><label>Item</label><designator>2.</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|12|32:12"><para.text>If the principal activities of a cooperative agricultural corporation are connected with the marketing, processing, manufacture, sale, or other dispositions of agricultural products, agricultural waste product, or agricultural compost, including the capture of methane and other gases for the generation and use or sale of energy, as defined in <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-energy" secref="103">&sect;1-103 of the N.Y. Energy Law</cite>, it may be termed a cooperative marketing corporation and incorporated as such. If its principal activities relate to the purchase of supplies for producers of agricultural products, it may be termed a cooperative purchasing association and incorporated as such, but, in either case such a corporation may engage in both such lines of activity. Nothing in <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" artref="6">Article 6 of the Cooperative Corporations Law</cite> or <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="112">&sect;112 of N.Y. Cooperative Corporations Law</cite> will be deemed to prohibit the incorporation of a cooperative corporation under Article 2 of the Cooperative Corporations Law or affect the existing powers of any existing cooperative corporation not within Section 111 of the Cooperative Corporations Law. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="112">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;112</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="61">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;61</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</item.reference>
<item.reference><name.block><label>Item</label><designator>4.</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|12|32:12"><para.text>Subject to any limitations provided by statute or in a certificate of incorporation, a corporation has the power, in furtherance of its corporate purposes, to have perpetual duration. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-buscorp" secref="202" subref="(a)" pararef="(1)">BCL &sect;202(a)(1)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="110">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;110</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</item.reference>
<item.reference><name.block><label>Item</label><designator>11.</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|12|32:12"><para.text>The certificate of incorporation must contain a designation of the Secretary of State as agent of the corporation for service of process and provide therein a post office address to which the Secretary of State can mail a copy of any process against the corporation served on the Secretary of State. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="11" subref="(10)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;11(10)</cite>.</para.text></para>

Corp. Law &sect;14(h), (i)</cite>.</para.text></para>

<item.reference><name.block><label>Item</label><designator>1.</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|13|32:13"><para.text>Where copy of certificate of incorporation was not included in record of shareholders&apos; action contesting their disqualification from voting for board of directors and where corporation&apos;s name did not include word &ldquo;cooperative,&rdquo; it was presumed that corporation was established under Business Corporation Law rather than Cooperative Corporations Law. <cite type="case">Yu v. Linton, 68 A.D.2d 856, 414 N.Y.S.2d 558 (1st Dep&apos;t 1979)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="164 to 179" secrange="y">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &dblsect;164 to 179</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</item.reference>
<item.reference><name.block><label>Item</label><designator>2.</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|13|32:13"><para.text>If the principal activities of a cooperative agricultural corporation are connected with the marketing, processing, manufacture, sale, or other dispositions of agricultural products, agricultural waste product, or agricultural compost including the capture of methane and other gases, for the generation and use or sale of energy, as defined in <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-energy" secref="1-103">&sect;1-103 of the N.Y. Energy Law</cite>, it may be termed a cooperative marketing corporation and incorporated as such. If its principal activities relate to the purchase of supplies for producers of agricultural products, it may be termed a cooperative purchasing association and incorporated as such, but in either case such a corporation may engage in both such lines of activity. Nothing in Article 6 or <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="112">&sect;112 of the N.Y. Cooperative Corporations Law</cite> will be deemed to prohibit the incorporation of a cooperative corporation under article two of this chapter or affect the existing powers of any existing cooperative corporation not within Section 111 of Article 6 of the Cooperative Corporations Law. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="112">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;112</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="61">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;61</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</item.reference>
<item.reference><name.block><label>Item</label><designator>3.</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|13|32:13"><para.text>Only persons engaged in the production of agricultural products or cooperative corporations of such producers organized under the laws of New York or any other state shall be eligible for membership in any agricultural marketing or purchasing corporation formed or operated under the provisions of this article. The terms and conditions of membership shall be prescribed in the bylaws. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="111" subref="(a)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;111(a)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|13|32:13"><para.text>Every cooperative corporation shall issue to each member, upon full payment therefor, a certificate of membership (whether evidenced by stock or otherwise) which shall not be transferable otherwise than as may be prescribed in this chapter, the certificate of incorporation, and bylaws. The corporation may accept as full or partial payment a member&apos;s promissory note but shall hold the certificate as security for payment, without, however, affecting the member&apos;s right to vote unless such note is past due. See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="40">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;40</cite>.</para.text></para>

<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="825">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;825</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>

<item.reference><name.block><label>Item</label><designator>6.</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|13|32:13"><para.text>For discussion of patronage dividends and other distributions, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="32:6">&sect;32:6</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alr3" titlename="Co-operative associations: rights in equity credits or patronage dividends" volref="50" pageref="435">Co-operative associations: rights in equity credits or patronage dividends, 50 A.L.R.3d 435</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</item.reference>
<item.reference><name.block><label>Item</label><designator>8.</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|13|32:13"><para.text>The board of directors must be chosen at the time and place and for terms fixed by the bylaws, but at least one-fourth of the directors must be elected annually. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="111" subref="(a)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;111(a)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|13|32:13"><para.text>A cooperative corporation may provide a fair remuneration for its directors and for members of its executive committee. No director or member of the executive committee shall be a party to a contract for profit with the corporation that in substance shall differ in any way from similar contracts by it with members or with others or that shall vary from terms generally current in the district. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="62">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;62</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|13|32:13"><para.text>Any member may bring charges against a director by filing them in writing with the secretary, together with a petition signed by 5&percnt; of the members, requesting removal. The corporation may thereupon remove the director by the affirmative vote of three-fourths of the members voting thereon at a meeting promptly held after due notice in writing, setting forth accurately the purpose for which such meeting is called, provided that at such meeting not less than 10&percnt; of the entire membership vote, personally or by mail. The director involved shall be given a copy of the charges reasonably in advance of the meeting, and he or she and the complainant shall have an opportunity at the meeting to be heard in person or by counsel and to present and cross-examine witnesses. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="63">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;63</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|13|32:13"><para.text>In case the bylaws provide for election of directors by districts with primary elections in each district, then the petition for removal of a director must be signed by 20&percnt; of the members residing in the district from which he or she was elected. The board of directors must call a special meeting of the members residing in that district to consider the removal of the director in the manner above provided, and, by a concurrent vote of a majority of the members of that district voting thereon, such director shall be removed from office. See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="63">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;63</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="545, 569, 791" secrange="y">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &dblsect;545, 569, 791</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</item.reference>
<item.reference><name.block><label>Item</label><designator>9.</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|13|32:13"><para.text>The corporation may provide a fair remuneration for its officers. No officer shall be a party to a contract for profit with the corporation that, in substance, shall differ in any way from similar contracts by it with members or with others or that shall vary from terms generally current in the district. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="62">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;62</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|13|32:13"><para.text>The officers of every cooperative corporation must include a president, one or more vice presidents, secretary, and treasurer who are required to be elected annually by the board of directors. The president and a first vice president must be members of the corporation or of a member corporation and must be elected from among the directors. Other officers need not be directors or members of the corporation. The offices of secretary and treasurer may be combined. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="64">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;64</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="532, 536, 789" secrange="y">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &dblsect;532, 536, 789</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</item.reference>
<item.reference><name.block><label>Item</label><designator>11.</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|13|32:13"><para.text>In accordance with provisions in the bylaws, any person will forfeit his or her membership upon proof that the person has ceased to be engaged in the occupation or occupations for the servicing of which the corporation was formed or has ceased to have the qualifications requisite for membership; in addition, the member must upon such notice and terms, as may be prescribed in the bylaws, surrender his or her membership certificate or shares of stock upon payment of the par or otherwise designated value thereof and of any accrued dividends thereon, as may appear in the accounting at the end of the current fiscal year. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="42">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;42</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="836">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;836</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</item.reference>
<item.reference><name.block><label>Item</label><designator>13.</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|13|32:13"><para.text>For an agricultural cooperative corporation, the bylaws may provide for their amendment by the board of directors, but any amendment adopted by the board that affects the preferential rights or obligations of the members or stockholders shall be reported to the next annual meeting of the corporation and, if not affirmatively approved thereat, shall cease to be in effect. Such bylaws reported to the annual meeting may be adopted, repealed, or amended on the affirmative vote of two-thirds of the members, stockholders, or delegates voting thereon at a meeting held after due written notice setting forth the proposed action and the purpose of the meeting. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="111" subref="(a)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;111(a)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="128">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;128</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</item.reference>
<item.reference><name.block><label>Item</label><designator>15.</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|13|32:13"><para.text>A cooperative corporation may, at any meeting and upon due and express notice previously given, by vote of two-thirds of all of the members or stockholders voting thereon, discontinue its operations and settle its affairs. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="17">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;17</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="1337, 1432" secrange="y">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &dblsect;1337, 1432</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</item.reference>
<item.reference><name.block><label>Item</label><designator>16(a).</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|13|32:13"><para.text>Before handling funds or securities of the corporation, amounting to &dollar;1,000 or more in any one year, the officer or employee shall be covered by an adequate bond to be approved by the board of directors. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="65">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;65</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="687">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;687</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</item.reference>
<item.reference><name.block><label>Item</label><designator>16(b).</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|13|32:13"><para.text>Immediately after the close of each fiscal year, every cooperative corporation shall cause an audit to be made of its operations for such fiscal year. A written report of the audit, including a statement of services rendered by the corporation, with total amount of business transacted, balance sheet, income, and expenses shall be submitted to the annual meeting of the corporation and shall at all times be available for inspection by any member. Such audit shall be made by an experienced bookkeeper or accountant or firm of accountants not regularly employed by the corporation, provided that in the case of a cooperative corporation, the annual business of which amounts to less than &dollar;100,000, the audit may be made by an auditing committee of three members or stockholders of the corporation who shall not be directors, officers, or employees thereof. Any person violating or failing to comply with the provisions of this section shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="75">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;75</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="379">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;379</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</item.reference>
</item.reference.block>

<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>32:14</designator><name>Checklist<sep/>Survey of matters considered by planning committee of poultry cooperative</name></outline.name.block>
<online.view>
<online.view.item>COL</online.view.item>
<online.view.item>NFP</online.view.item>
<online.view.item>CHK</online.view.item>
<online.view.item>FCV</online.view.item>
<online.view.item>FTR</online.view.item>
<online.view.item>EBL</online.view.item>
</online.view>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<form uuid="Ia3929dd0181a11e68738d3db3a7c8dd3">
<tbl ident="NYLB:32-14_001">
<table resize="minus1">
<tgroup align="left" cols="5">
<colspec colname="1" colnum="1" colwidth="1*"/>
<colspec colname="2" colnum="2" colwidth="1*"/>
<colspec colname="3" colnum="3" colwidth="4*"/>
<colspec colname="4" colnum="4" colwidth="1*"/>
<colspec colname="5" colnum="5" colwidth="1*"/>
<tbody>
<row><entry>I. Operating Costs and Volume of Business:</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">1. How much will the operating costs be and how will they be met? In answering, consider the following costs:</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">&bull;</entry><entry>Rental</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="3">&ballot;&lsqb;&rsqb; Monthly rent</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">&bull;</entry><entry>Salaries per month:</entry></row>
<row><entry>&emsp;</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="3">&ballot;&lsqb;&rsqb; Manager</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="3">&ballot;&lsqb;&rsqb; Delivery</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="3">&ballot;&lsqb;&rsqb; Candlers</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="3">&ballot;&lsqb;&rsqb; Clerk</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="3">&ballot;&lsqb;&rsqb; Pickup</entry></row>
<row><entry>&emsp;</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">&bull;</entry><entry>Other costs per month:</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="3">&ballot;&lsqb;&rsqb; Trucks (operation and depreciation)</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="3">&ballot;&lsqb;&rsqb; Electricity, water, telephone</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="3">&ballot;&lsqb;&rsqb; Supplies (fillers and flats&mdash;cases)</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="3">&ballot;&lsqb;&rsqb; Seals</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="3">&ballot;&lsqb;&rsqb; Taxes</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="3">&ballot;&lsqb;&rsqb; Workers&apos; compensation insurance</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="3">&ballot;&lsqb;&rsqb; Operating expenses&mdash;manager</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="3">&ballot;&lsqb;&rsqb; Audit</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="3">&ballot;&lsqb;&rsqb; All others cost</entry></row>
<row><entry>&emsp;</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">2. What is the necessary business volume needed to meet these costs? In answering, please consider:</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">&bull;</entry><entry>What is the least volume necessary to meet overhead costs?</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">&bull;</entry><entry>Are there enough producers willing to join a cooperative to guarantee the minimum volume?</entry></row>
<row><entry>&emsp;</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">3. How should supplies bought by members be treated. In answering, please consider:</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">&bull;</entry><entry>What will be the policy on purchasing supplies for members?</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">&bull;</entry><entry>Price to members?</entry></row>
<row><entry>&emsp;</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="3">What will be the policy on purchasing supplies for members? Price to members? Delivery to members?</entry></row>
<row><entry>&emsp;</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">4. How should delivery of member produce be handled? In answering, please consider:</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">&bull;</entry><entry>Will members&apos; produce be picked up at the farm?</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">&bull;</entry><entry>Will members&apos; produce be delivered to cooperative?</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">&bull;</entry><entry>Will members&apos; produce be delivered to buyers?</entry></row>
<row><entry>&emsp;</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">5. How much capital will be required? In answering, please consider:</entry></row>
<row><entry>&bull;</entry><entry colname="3">Cost of fixed capital:</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="3">&ballot;&lsqb;&rsqb; Pickup truck</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="3">&ballot;&lsqb;&rsqb; Stake 1 1/2 ton</entry></row>
<row><entry>&bull;</entry><entry colname="3">Office equipment:</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="3">&ballot;&lsqb;&rsqb; Computers</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="3">&ballot;&lsqb;&rsqb; Desk</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="3">&ballot;&lsqb;&rsqb; Photocopy machine</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="3">&ballot;&lsqb;&rsqb; File cabinet and supplies</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="3">&ballot;&lsqb;&rsqb; Sizing machine</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="3">&ballot;&lsqb;&rsqb; Chill room</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">&bull;</entry><entry>Miscellaneous</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="3">&ballot;&lsqb;&rsqb; Record books and set up&mdash;co-op books</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="3">&ballot;&lsqb;&rsqb; Attorney&apos;s fees</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="3">&ballot;&lsqb;&rsqb; Recording fee</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="3">&ballot;&lsqb;&rsqb; Retainer fee (lawyer)</entry></row>
<row><entry>&emsp;</entry></row>
<row><entry>II. Outlets and Proposed Marketing Methods:</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">1. Often it is advisable to confine marketing operations to one trade group, i.e., retailers or wholesalers. Trying to sell to several groups may arouse antagonism from one or other of established business groups. What should the committee suggest in this respect?</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">2. What reception should the cooperative expect from potential customers and competitors now in business?</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">3. Will the cooperative establish its own place of business with a complete sales and delivery force, or will it employ an agent on a contract basis?</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">4. Will the policy be to market a uniform product that can be standardized under supervision of the cooperative management, and labeled and advertised as a cooperative product, or to act as an agent for produce packed on the members&apos; farms?</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">5. What will be price policy on sales?</entry></row>
<row><entry>III. Organization and financing:</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">1. Where will the place, or places, of business be established?</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">2. What should the scope of the cooperative be? How many products will the cooperative attempt to handle at the beginning? Later?</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">3. From how big an area will members be accepted? The state? One country? One district?</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">4. What should the name of the cooperative be?</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">5. Financing: Will the cooperative be incorporated or not? Will it be a stock organization by which capital is raised from the sale of interest-bearing stock certificates, or a nonstock cooperative that requires only membership fees? Usually this is decided by the amount of capital required.</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">6. Membership: Will there be any limitation on the least volume of business that possible members will give to the cooperatives?</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">7. How many potential members are there, and how many of them will join a cooperative?</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">8. What will be the membership fee?</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">9. What plan is proposed to secure maximum membership?</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">10. Will the cooperative do business with nonmembers? To what extent?</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">11. How will the Board of Directors be chosen? On the basis of size of business, by districts, at large, or a combination? What fees and expenses will be paid to Directors?</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">12. Manager: What type of manager will be employed? At what salary? What will his or her duties and authority be in relation to the Board of Directors?</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">13. What reports will the manager and Board of Directors give to members? How often?</entry></row>
<row><entry>IV. Marketing Agreement:</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">1. To establish a new business there must usually be a guarantee of a certain volume of business. How shall member contracts of volume be made? On an estimated quantity per month? Or a percentage of total production?</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">2. Meeting the cost of operating a business requires certain deductions from gross returns. Shall deductions be on a fee per unit sold or on a percentage of dollar sales?</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">3. How long a period shall the marketing agreement cover?</entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">4. What will be the penalties for noncompliance of members? What escape clauses will be allowed members in the contract? What escape clauses for the cooperative?</entry></row>
</tbody>
</tgroup>
</table>
</tbl>

<form uuid="Ia3931300181a11e68738d3db3a7c8dd3">
<form.name.block><name>ORGANIZATION AGREEMENT</name></form.name.block>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|15|32:15"><form.text>The undersigned, a producer of agricultural products, referred to as the &ldquo;Producer,&rdquo; together with other signers of agreements similar to this agreement, for the purpose of engaging in <inline.instr>&lsqb;list of purposes for organization&rsqb;</inline.instr>, propose to organize an agricultural cooperative association without capital stock under the laws of the State of New York, as provided in this agreement. The undersigned agrees, both for the undersigned and for the express benefit of the association to be organized, as follows:</form.text></form.para>
<form.unit>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>1</designator><name>ORGANIZATION COMMITTEE</name></name.block></head>
<form.unit>
<form.item><name.block><designator>(a)</designator></name.block><form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|15|32:15"><form.text>The association will be organized with a suitable certificate of incorporation and bylaws as determined by an organization committee consisting of the following persons: <inline.instr>&lsqb;names of committee members&rsqb;</inline.instr> and <inline.instr>&lsqb;addresses of committee members&rsqb;</inline.instr>.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><name.block><designator>(b)</designator></name.block><form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|15|32:15"><form.text>This committee may, in the discretion of a majority of its members, increase its membership, fill any committee vacancy, and appoint any committees deemed necessary to conduct the details of its affairs. The committee or any committee designated by it may prescribe an organization fee to be paid by each person signing an organization agreement similar to this document and may incur necessary obligations, make necessary expenditures, and take any such action as may, in its discretion, be deemed advisable to further the organization of the association.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
</form.unit></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>2</designator><name>BYLAWS</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|15|32:15"><form.text>The bylaws of the association will provide, among other things, that <inline.instr>&lsqb;enumeration of principal proposed provisions&rsqb;</inline.instr>.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>3</designator><name>ORGANIZATIONAL MEETING</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|15|32:15"><form.text>If, on or before <inline.instr>&lsqb;date of notice&rsqb;</inline.instr>, the organization committee is of the opinion that sufficient sign-up has been obtained to enable the association to function effectively, the committee will, by notice to be published in one or more newspapers of general circulation in the area in which those who sign the agreements like this one reside, specify a date and a place for a meeting of those who sign such agreements to enable those attending such meeting to conclusively determine, by majority vote, if a sufficient sign-up has been obtained to justify the formation and operation of the association, and to consider such other business as may be deemed expedient. Notice of the action there taken will be published in one or more newspapers of general circulation in the area.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>4</designator><name>ACCOUNTING OF RECEIPTS AND EXPENDITURES</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|15|32:15"><form.text>The organization committee will keep full, true, and detailed accounts of all receipts and of all expenditures of every kind; will have the accounts audited; will render a written report of the audit to the board of directors of the association when organized; and will thereupon turn over to the association any balance remaining in its hands free of obligation. If the association is not so organized, the unexpended balance of the account will be prorated to those who contributed to it.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>5</designator><name>REVOLVING FUND CERTIFICATES</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|15|32:15"><form.text>Producer subscribes for <inline.instr>&lsqb;number of revolving fund certificates&rsqb;</inline.instr> revolving fund certificates, each of the face value of &dollar;<inline.instr>&lsqb;dollar amount of face value&rsqb;</inline.instr>, and agrees to pay for the certificates as follows: <inline.instr>&lsqb;terms of payment&rsqb;</inline.instr>.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>6</designator><name>APPLICATION FOR MEMBERSHIP; SIGNATURE OF MARKETING AGREEMENT</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|15|32:15"><form.text>Producer applies for membership in the association when organized and expressly agrees that signature to the marketing agreement will be deemed, to all intents and purposes, the same as signature to this organization agreement, all of which shall be irrevocable, except as provided in Paragraph 3 of this organization agreement and Paragraph <inline.instr>&lsqb;designation of paragraph&rsqb;</inline.instr> of the marketing agreement or the association&apos;s bylaws, and Producer so agrees in order to induce other producers to sign agreements such as this for Producer&apos;s benefit as well as for their own general benefit.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>7</designator><name>NOTICE OF ACCEPTANCE</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|15|32:15"><form.text>Acceptance of this agreement will be deemed conclusive on the mailing, by the association, of a notice to that effect to Producer at Producer&apos;s address noted below, and such mailing and notice will be conclusively established by the affidavit of the secretary of the corporation.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>8</designator><name>MARKETING AGREEMENT</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|15|32:15"><form.text>Subject to the terms of this agreement, Producer agrees to be bound by the terms of the following marketing agreement, which, on its acceptance by the corporation, may be used separately apart from this organization agreement: <inline.instr>&lsqb;recitation of marketing agreement terms&rsqb;</inline.instr>.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
</form.unit>
<form.line align="l">Dated: <inline.instr>&lsqb;date of agreement&rsqb;</inline.instr>, at <inline.instr>&lsqb;name of city&rsqb;</inline.instr>, New York.</form.line>
<signature.block ref="manual">
<signature.group position="r">
<form.vertical.space amt="1"/>
<form.line align="l" lineover="y"><inline.instr>&lsqb;Name of producer&rsqb;</inline.instr></form.line>
<form.line align="l"><inline.instr>&lsqb;Address of producer&rsqb;</inline.instr></form.line>
<form.line align="l">Accepted: <inline.instr>&lsqb;date of acceptance&rsqb;</inline.instr></form.line>
<form.vertical.space amt="1"/>
<form.line align="l" lineover="y"><inline.instr>&lsqb;Names of other parties&rsqb;</inline.instr></form.line>
</signature.group>
</signature.block>
<note.block>
<note.group note.head="none">
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|15|32:15"><para.text>An alternative to publishing the actions taken at the organization meeting may be to provide that the proposed organization will not be organized unless a certain proportion of the acreage or tonnage within a certain district is signed up. A further provision is then generally made that the certificate of the organization committee to the effect that the required acreage or tonnage has been signed will be conclusive.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|15|32:15"><para.text>At the first meeting of the corporation, bylaws are required to be adopted, by a majority vote of the members or by their written assent, to regulate the conduct and management of the corporation. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-buscorp" secref="601" subref="(a)">BCL &sect;601(a)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|15|32:15"><para.text>The terms and conditions of membership in an agricultural corporation must be prescribed in the bylaws. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="111" subref="(a)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;111(a)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|15|32:15"><para.text>The term &ldquo;agricultural products&rdquo; includes horticultural, viticultural, dairy, livestock, poultry, bee, and any farm products. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="111" subref="(b)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;111(b)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|15|32:15"><para.text>Any five or more producers of agricultural products may form a cooperative agricultural corporation, either with or without capital stock. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="112">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;112</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|15|32:15"><para.text>For other forms of subscription agreements, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="17:1 et seq." secrange="y">&dblsect;17:1 et seq.</cite></para.text></para>
</note.group>

<form uuid="Ia3933a10181a11e68738d3db3a7c8dd3">
<form.name.block><name>REVOLVING FUND CERTIFICATE SERIES</name></form.name.block>
<tbl ident="NYLB:32-16_001">
<table>
<tgroup align="left" cols="2">
<colspec colname="1" colnum="1" colwidth="1*"/>
<colspec colname="2" colnum="2" colwidth="19*"/>
<tbody>
<row><entry>No.</entry><entry><inline.instr>&lsqb;Number of certificate&rsqb;</inline.instr></entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2"><inline.instr>&lsqb;Date of certificate&rsqb;</inline.instr></entry></row>
<row><entry colname="2">&dollar;<inline.instr>&lsqb;Dollar amount of certificate&rsqb;</inline.instr></entry></row>
</tbody>
</tgroup>
</table>
</tbl>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|16|32:16"><form.text>This certifies that <inline.instr>&lsqb;name of member&rsqb;</inline.instr>, of <inline.instr>&lsqb;address of member&rsqb;</inline.instr>, <inline.instr>&lsqb;name of city&rsqb;</inline.instr>, <inline.instr>&lsqb;name of county&rsqb;</inline.instr>, <inline.instr>&lsqb;name of state&rsqb;</inline.instr>, has furnished &dollar;<inline.instr>&lsqb;dollar amount of capital&rsqb;</inline.instr> to this corporation as capital subject to the following conditions:</form.text></form.para>
<form.unit>
<form.item><name.block><designator>1</designator></name.block><form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|16|32:16"><form.text>This and other revolving fund certificates of the same series may be retired in the sole discretion of the board of directors, either fully or on a pro rata basis, but certificates issued in prior years will be entitled to priority (except as provided in this document) in retirement.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><name.block><designator>2</designator></name.block><form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|16|32:16"><form.text>The amount stated in this certificate will bear only such rate of interest, if any, as the board of directors may fix, from time to time, in no event to exceed <inline.instr>&lsqb;percentage rate of annual interest&rsqb;</inline.instr>&percnt; per year.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><name.block><designator>3</designator></name.block><form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|16|32:16"><form.text>This certificate is transferable only on the books of the corporation.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><name.block><designator>4</designator></name.block><form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|16|32:16"><form.text>This and other certificates are subject in all respects to the corporation&apos;s bylaws and are junior and subordinate to all debts of the corporation, both secured and unsecured.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
</form.unit>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|16|32:16"><form.text>Upon the winding up or liquidation of the corporation in any manner, after full payment of all of its creditors, all revolving fund certificates will then be retired in full or on a pro rata basis, without priority.</form.text></form.para>

<note.block>
<note.group note.head="taxnotes">
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|17|32:17"><para.text>Unlike other nonspecific types of cooperative organizations, an agricultural cooperative is defined with precision by the Code, regulations, rulings, and cases. Two kinds of agricultural co-ops qualify as &ldquo;tax-exempt.&rdquo; The term is placed in quotes for a reason. While these organizations are stated to be &ldquo;exempt from taxation&rdquo; under <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="521">26 U.S.C.A. &dblsect;521</cite>, farmers&apos; cooperatives are still required to be pay taxes specified in <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1381 et seq." secrange="y">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1381 et seq.</cite>, <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="1381">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;1381</cite> then requires them to pay the ordinary income tax and capital gains tax levied by. 26 U.S.C.A. &dblsect;11 and 1201. Section 1381 then goes on to say that in spite of these taxes being levied against agricultural cooperatives, they are considered to be exempt from income taxes for any purpose in which the law refers to exempt organizations.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|17|32:17"><para.text>The two types of agricultural cooperatives that are recognized are the marketing co-op and the purchasing co-op. The requirements for these organizations are found at <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="521" subref="(b)" pararef="(1), (4)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;521(b)(1), (4)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|17|32:17"><para.text>The result is that an agricultural cooperative is entitled to a special deduction for patronage dividends, dividends on capital stock, and certain other distributions. Otherwise, they pay tax under the regular rules that relate to ordinary income and capital gain. They are not permitted the dividends-received deduction and may not use the consolidated return provisions. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.522-1" subref="(a)">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.522-1(a)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|17|32:17"><para.text>For a discussion of considerations relevant to the drafting of certificates of incorporation, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="32:9">&sect;32:9</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|17|32:17"><para.text>For a discussion of the formal requirements of certificates of incorporation, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="32:10, 32:12" secrange="y">&dblsect;32:10, 32:12</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|17|32:17"><para.text>In Article II, the description of the purpose for incorporation could include: to engage in any cooperative activity in connection with the producing, marketing, or selling of agricultural products, as that term is defined in <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="111" subref="(b)">N.Y Cooperative Corporations Law &sect;111(b)</cite>, and in general to function as an agricultural cooperative corporation within the meaning of <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="111" subref="(a)">N.Y Cooperative Corporations Law &sect;111(a)</cite>, to which end the return on the stock or membership capital of the corporation shall be limited to 12&percnt; per year and the value of business done with nonmembers in any fiscal year shall not exceed the value of business done with members during such fiscal year.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|17|32:17"><para.text>The certificate of incorporation must include the purposes of the corporation, which are required to be consistent with the New York Cooperative Corporations Law. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="11" subref="(2)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;11(2)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|17|32:17"><para.text>For the purposes for which a general cooperative corporation may be formed, see <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="13">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;13</cite>; for the more specific purposes of an agricultural cooperative corporation, see <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="110">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;110</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|17|32:17"><para.text>Any five or more producers of agricultural products may form a cooperative agricultural corporation, either with or without capital stock, by subscribing and filing a certificate of incorporation. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="112">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;112</cite>. The certificate of incorporation must be acknowledged by all the incorporators. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="11">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;11</cite>.</para.text></para>
</note.group>
<research.reference.block>

<item.reference.block>
<item.reference><name.block><label>ARTICLE</label><designator>I.</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|17|32:17"><para.text>A certificate of incorporation is required to set forth the name of the corporation, which must include the word &ldquo;Cooperative.&rdquo; <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="11" subref="(1)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;11(1)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="164 to 179" secrange="y">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &dblsect;164 to 179</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</item.reference>
<item.reference><name.block><label>ARTICLE</label><designator>II.</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|17|32:17"><para.text>The certificate of incorporation is required to set forth the purposes for which the corporation has been formed. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="11" subref="(2)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;11(2)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|17|32:17"><para.text>The powers of cooperative corporations are delineated in <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="14">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;14</cite>. If desired, these powers may be incorporated into the purpose section of the certificate of incorporation.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="61">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;61</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</item.reference>
<item.reference><name.block><label>ARTICLE</label><designator>III.</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|17|32:17"><para.text>The certificate of incorporation is required to designate the Secretary of State as an agent of the corporation for the purpose of receiving process that may be served on the corporation. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="11" subref="(10)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;11(10)</cite>. If the corporation is to have a registered agent, the certificate of incorporation must include the agent&apos;s name and address within New York and a statement that he or she is authorized to receive process served against the corporation. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="11" subref="(11)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;11(11)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="73">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;73</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="1062, 1063" secrange="y">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &dblsect;1062, 1063</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</item.reference>
<item.reference><name.block><label>ARTICLE</label><designator>IV.</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|17|32:17"><para.text>The certificate of incorporation must state the term for which the corporation is to exist. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="11" subref="(3)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;11(3)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|17|32:17"><para.text>Subject to any limitations provided by statute or in a certificate of incorporation, a corporation has the power, in furtherance of its corporate purposes, to have perpetual duration. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-buscorp" secref="202" subref="(a)" pararef="(1)">BCL &sect;202(a)(1)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="110">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;110</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</item.reference>
<item.reference><name.block><label>ARTICLE</label><designator>V.</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|17|32:17"><para.text>A certificate of incorporation is required to set forth the names and post office addresses of the incorporators. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="11" subref="(5)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;11(5)</cite>.</para.text></para>
</item.reference>
<item.reference><name.block><label>ARTICLE</label><designator>VI.</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|17|32:17"><para.text>If the corporation is organized with capital stock, the certificate of incorporation must state the total amount of such stock, the total number, if any, of the shares without par value, and the total number and par value of any shares having a par value, and, if the shares are to be classified, the number of shares to be included in each class and all of the designations, preferences, privileges, and voting rights or restrictions and qualifications of the shares of each class. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="11" subref="(8)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;11(8)</cite>.</para.text></para>
</item.reference>
</item.reference.block>

<section.body>
<form uuid="Ia39499a0181a11e68738d3db3a7c8dd3">
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|21|32:21"><form.text>The shares of the corporation shall consist of <inline.instr>&lsqb;total number of shares&rsqb;</inline.instr> shares divided into <inline.instr>&lsqb;number of shares&rsqb;</inline.instr> shares of <inline.instr>&lsqb;specification of stock&rsqb;</inline.instr> stock of the par value of &dollar;<inline.instr>&lsqb;dollar amount of par value&rsqb;</inline.instr> per share, and <inline.instr>&lsqb;number of shares&rsqb;</inline.instr> shares of <inline.instr>&lsqb;specification of stock&rsqb;</inline.instr> stock of the par value of &dollar;<inline.instr>&lsqb;dollar amount of par value&rsqb;</inline.instr> per share.</form.text></form.para>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|21|32:21"><form.text>The board of directors may, subject to the approval of a majority of the members, fix the dividend rate, the conversion rights, the voting rights, the redemption price, and the liquidation preferences of any wholly unissued class of shares, or all or any of them.</form.text></form.para>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|21|32:21"><form.text>The shares of preferred stock may be reduced at such redemption price and bear such particular designation as the board of directors shall by resolution determine and fix prior to the issuance of such shares.</form.text></form.para>
<note.block>
<note.group note.head="taxnotes">
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|21|32:21"><para.text>Farmers&apos; cooperatives need not issue capital stock but are not penalized for doing so. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="521" subref="(b)" pararef="(2)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;521(b)(2)</cite>. Dividends on the stock must, however, be limited to the legal rate of interest or 8&percnt;, whichever is greater. In addition, substantially all the stock must be owned by &ldquo;producers who market their products or purchase their supplies and equipment&rdquo; through the cooperative. Distributions on the stock are deductible by the cooperative against its income.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|21|32:21"><para.text>If the corporation is organized with stock, the certificate must state the total amount of such stock, the total number, if any, of the shares without par value, and the total number and par value of any shares having a par value. If the shares are to be classified, it must also state the number of shares to be included in each class and all of the designations, preferences, privileges, and voting rights or restrictions and qualifications of the shares of each class. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="11" subref="(8)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;11(8)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|21|32:21"><para.text>Dividends payable on all classes of preferred stock may not exceed 12&percnt; per year. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="111" subref="(a)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;111(a)</cite>.</para.text></para>
</note.group>

<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>32:22</designator><name>Certificate of incorporation<sep/>Provision<sep/>Limitation of personal liability of board of directors</name></outline.name.block>
<online.view>
<online.view.item>CLS</online.view.item>
<online.view.item>COL</online.view.item>
<online.view.item>FCV</online.view.item>
<online.view.item>FTR</online.view.item>
<online.view.item>COR</online.view.item>
<online.view.item>TEM</online.view.item>
<online.view.item>MTD</online.view.item>
</online.view>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<form uuid="Ia394e7c0181a11e68738d3db3a7c8dd3">
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|22|32:22"><form.text>No director of this cooperative shall be personally liable to this cooperative or its members for monetary damages for breach of fiduciary duty as a director, except for liability:</form.text></form.para>
<form.unit>
<form.item><name.block><designator>(a)</designator></name.block><form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|22|32:22"><form.text>For a breach of the director&apos;s duty of loyalty to this cooperative or its members;</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><name.block><designator>(b)</designator></name.block><form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|22|32:22"><form.text>For acts or omissions not in good faith or that involve intentional misconduct or a knowing violation of law;</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><name.block><designator>(c)</designator></name.block><form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|22|32:22"><form.text>For a transaction from which the director derived an improper personal benefit; or</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><name.block><designator>(d)</designator></name.block><form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|22|32:22"><form.text>For an act or omission occurring prior to the date when the provisions of this Article (or predecessor thereto) became effective.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
</form.unit>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|22|32:22"><form.text>It is the intention of the members of this cooperative to eliminate or limit the personal liability of the directors of this cooperative to the greatest extent permitted under <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-buscorp" secref="402" subref="(b)">Section 402(b) of the New York Business Corporation Law</cite>. If amendments to that section or other law are passed after the effective date of this Article, which authorize cooperatives to act to further limit or eliminate the personal liability of directors, then the liability of the directors of this cooperative shall be limited or eliminated to the greatest extent permitted by such statute as amended. Any repeal or modification of this Article by the members of this cooperative shall not adversely affect any right of or any protection available to a director of this cooperative that is in existence at the time of such repeal or modification.</form.text></form.para>
<note.block>
<note.group note.head="none">
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|22|32:22"><para.text>The certificate of incorporation may set forth a provision eliminating or limiting the personal liability of directors to the corporation or its shareholders for damages for any breach of duty in such capacity, provided that no such provision shall eliminate or limit:</para.text>
<list list.style="para">
<list.item><name.block><designator>(1)</designator></name.block><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|22|32:22"><para.text>the liability of any director if a judgment or other final adjudication adverse to him or her establishes that his or her acts or omissions were in bad faith or involved intentional misconduct or a knowing violation of law or that he or she personally gained in fact a financial profit or other advantage to which he or she was not legally entitled or that his or her acts violated <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-buscorp" secref="719">Section 719 of the Business Corporation Law</cite>; or</para.text></para></list.item>
<list.item><name.block><designator>(2)</designator></name.block><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|22|32:22"><para.text>the liability of any director for any act or omission prior to the adoption of a provision authorized by this paragraph.</para.text></para></list.item>
</list></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|22|32:22"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-buscorp" secref="402" subref="(b)">BCL &sect;402(b)</cite>.</para.text></para>
</note.group>
