<front>
<outline.name.block>
<designator>A</designator><name>General Considerations</name></outline.name.block>
</front>
<analytical.level.body>
<section.block>
<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>32:48</designator><name>Introduction</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Agriculture" numref="6">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Agriculture &key;6</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Associations" numref="128">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Associations &key;128</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Associations" numref="129">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Associations &key;129</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|50|32:48"><para.text>In New York, specific statutory provisions authorize marketing contracts between a cooperative corporation and its members, under which the members are required to sell all or any specified portion of any product or specified commodity exclusively to or through the corporation or facilities created by the corporation.<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|50|32:48"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="70" subref="(1)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;70(1)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> Such contracts may obligate the members during any designated period of time, subject to the right of each member to be released at a designated period in each year, by giving a prescribed notice.<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|50|32:48"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="70" subref="(1)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;70(1)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> These contracts are expressly declared not to be illegal or in restraint of trade.<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|50|32:48"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-genbus" secref="340" subref="(3)">GBL &sect;340(3)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Exemption of cooperatives from state antimonopoly laws, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Trade Regulation" secref="23">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Trade Regulation &sect;23</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|50|32:48"><para.text>The state laws relating to the restraint and prevention of monopolies do not apply to cooperative associations, corporate or otherwise, of farmers, gardeners, or dairymen, including livestock farmers and fruit growers, or to contracts, agreements, or arrangements made by such associations.<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|50|32:48"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-genbus" secref="340" subref="(3)">GBL &sect;340(3)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Exemption of cooperatives from state antimonopoly laws, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Trade Regulation" secref="23">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Trade Regulation &sect;23</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|50|32:48"><para.text>Persons engaged in the production of agricultural products may act together in associations, corporate or otherwise, with or without capital stock, in collectively processing, preparing for market, handling, and marketing in interstate or foreign commerce products of persons so engaged.<footnote><footnote.reference>5</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|50|32:48"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="110">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;110</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Agricultural cooperative corporations, generally, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="30">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;30</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> Such corporations and their members are further authorized to make the necessary contracts and agreements to effect these purposes.<footnote><footnote.reference>6</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|50|32:48"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="14">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;14</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> However, these corporations are subject to requirements that they be operated for the members&apos; mutual benefit, that they do not deal in the products of nonmembers to an amount greater in value than the amount handled for members, that no member of the corporation be allowed more than one vote regardless of the amount of stock or membership capital he or she may own in the corporation, and that the corporations do not pay dividends on stock or membership in excess of 12&percnt; per year.<footnote><footnote.reference>7</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|50|32:48"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="111">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;111</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Power of cooperatives to conduct business, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="473, 474" secrange="y">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &dblsect;473, 474</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|50|32:48"><para.text>The marketing contract may provide that the corporation may sell or resell the products delivered by its members, with or without taking title to such products, and may pay over to its members the resale price or the pool price, in case of pooling of sales, after deducting all necessary selling, overhead, and other costs and expenses, including interest or distribution on stock, not exceeding 6&percnt; per year, and any other deductions authorized by the bylaws or marketing contract.<footnote><footnote.reference>8</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|50|32:48"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="70" subref="(4)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;70(4)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Agricultural cooperative corporations, generally, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="30">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;30</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|50|32:48"><para.text>The marketing agreement may fix specific sums as liquidated damages, which sums will not be regarded as penalties, payable for breach by a member or shareholder or contracting nonmember of the marketing obligation.<footnote><footnote.reference>9</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|50|32:48"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="70" subref="(2)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;70(2)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Provision for liquidated damages with respect to marketing contracts, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="478">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;478</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Liquidated damage provision in marketing contracts, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="aj2" topicname="Cooperative Associations" secref="46">Am. Jur. 2d, Cooperative Associations &sect;46</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> A provision of this type may also be placed in the certificate of incorporation or bylaws.<footnote><footnote.reference>10</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|50|32:48"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="70" subref="(2)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;70(2)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Provision for liquidated damages with respect to marketing contracts, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="478">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;478</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Liquidated damage provision in marketing contracts, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="aj2" topicname="Cooperative Associations" secref="46">Am. Jur. 2d, Cooperative Associations &sect;46</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|50|32:48"><para.text>It may be further provided that a member or shareholder will pay all costs, premiums for bonds, expenses, and fees in case the corporation recovers judgment in any action on the marketing contract.<footnote><footnote.reference>11</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|50|32:48"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="70" subref="(2)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;70(2)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Provision for liquidated damages with respect to marketing contracts, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="478">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;478</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> A corporation is also given the right, in the event of a breach or threatened breach of a marketing contract by a member or by a contracting nonmember, to enjoin further breach of the contract and to obtain a decree of specific performance to enforce the contract.<footnote><footnote.reference>12</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|50|32:48"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="70" subref="(3)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;70(3)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Right of cooperative to injunction and specific performance with respect to marketing contracts, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="479">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;479</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Injunction and specific performance to enforce marketing contracts, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="aj2" topicname="Cooperative Associations" secref="44">Am. Jur. 2d, Cooperative Associations &sect;44</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> Upon the filing of a verified complaint showing a breach of the marketing agreement and of a bond approved by the court, the corporation is entitled to a temporary restraining order.<footnote><footnote.reference>13</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|50|32:48"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="70" subref="(3)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;70(3)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Right of cooperative to injunction and specific performance with respect to marketing contracts, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="479">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;479</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Injunction and specific performance to enforce marketing contracts, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="aj2" topicname="Cooperative Associations" secref="44">Am. Jur. 2d, Cooperative Associations &sect;44</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
</section.body>
</section>
<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>32:49</designator><name>Form drafting principles</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Agriculture" numref="6">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Agriculture &key;6</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Associations" numref="128">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Associations &key;128</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Associations" numref="129">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Associations &key;129</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|51|32:49"><para.text>To be effective, a marketing contract must satisfy such basic requirements of all contracts as competent parties who express definite assent in the form required, sufficient consideration, and a legal object or purpose.<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Validity and binding effect of marketing contracts, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="aj2" topicname="Cooperative Associations" secref="31">Am. Jur. 2d, Cooperative Associations &sect;31</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|51|32:49"><para.text>A marketing contract, due to its complexity, should always be in writing and should observe formalities that are often omitted in the simpler forms of contract. Because such contracts are construed strictly, extreme care should be taken to avoid any ambiguities in the contract&apos;s provisions.<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Power of cooperatives to enter into marketing contracts, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="477 to 481" secrange="y">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &dblsect;477 to 481</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Marketing contracts, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="aj2" topicname="Cooperative Associations" secref="30 to 48" secrange="y">Am. Jur. 2d, Cooperative Associations &dblsect;30 to 48</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<feature.para.block><name.block><name>Practice Tip:</name></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|51|32:49"><para.text>Marketing contracts are sometimes attached to preorganization agreements in order that they may be signed by prospective members prior to incorporation of the cooperative. In such circumstances, the marketing agreement is executed contemporaneously by the prospective member with the execution of the organization agreement and as a part of the entire contract.</para.text></para>
</feature.para.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|51|32:49"><para.text>Marketing contracts entered into prior to the formation of a producers&apos; marketing corporation are valid and binding upon the producers as signers after the formation of the corporation.<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|51|32:49"><para.text>See <cite type="case">Castorland Milk &amp; Cheese Co. v. Shantz, 179 N.Y.S. 131 (Sup 1919)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<feature.para.block><name.block><name>Practice Tip:</name></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|51|32:49"><para.text>A cooperative marketing agreement may create either of two relationships with respect to the products to be marketed under it: (1) a relationship of buyer and seller (a sales contract); or (2) the relationship of principal and agent between the member and the association (an agency contract). The nature of the relationship and the type of contract created depends upon the intention of the parties, as evidenced by the provisions of the contract, and as viewed in the light of the articles of incorporation or charter, the bylaws, and the circumstances of the particular case, including applicable statutory provisions.<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|51|32:49"><para.text>See <cite type="case">Pyrke v. Brudno, 243 A.D. 493, 278 N.Y.S. 353 (3d Dep&apos;t 1935), aff&apos;d, 269 N.Y. 652, 200 N.E. 42 (1936)</cite> (milk producers&apos; cooperative contract to sell milk to a milk dealer was one of agency and not of purchase and sale).</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Nature of, and relationship created by, marketing agreement, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="aj2" topicname="Cooperative Associations" secref="35">Am. Jur. 2d, Cooperative Associations &sect;35</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
</feature.para.block>
</section.body>
</section>

<list list.style="para">
<list.item><name.block><designator>(a)</designator></name.block><para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|52|32:50"><para.text>Entire agreement between parties.</para.text></para></list.item>

<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Associations" numref="129">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Associations &key;129</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
<item.reference.block>
<item.reference><name.block><label>Item</label><designator>1.</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|52|32:50"><para.text>The parties to the contract should be clearly identified and have the capacity to contract.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Contracts" secref="25, 26" secrange="y">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Contracts &dblsect;25, 26</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</item.reference>
<item.reference><name.block><label>Item</label><designator>3.</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|52|32:50"><para.text>A cooperative marketing agreement may create either of two relationships with respect to the products to be marketed under it: (1) a relationship of buyer and seller (a sales contract); or (2) the relationship of principal and agent between the member and the association (an agency contract). The nature of the relationship and the type of contract created depends upon the intention of the parties, as evidenced by the provisions of the contract, and as viewed in the light of the articles of incorporation or charter, the bylaws, and the circumstances of the particular case, including applicable statutory provisions. See <cite type="case">Pyrke v. Brudno, 243 A.D. 493, 278 N.Y.S. 353 (3d Dep&apos;t 1935), aff&apos;d, 269 N.Y. 652, 200 N.E. 42 (1936)</cite> (milk producers&apos; cooperative contract to sell milk to a milk dealer was one of agency and not of purchase and sale). Using this checklist provision would clearly create a sales contract.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="aj2" topicname="Cooperative Associations" secref="35">Am. Jur. 2d, Cooperative Associations &sect;35</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</item.reference>
<item.reference><name.block><label>Item</label><designator>4.</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|52|32:50"><para.text>As a contract of sale, the provisions of the New York Uniform Commercial Code would apply to the provisions concerning the place and time of delivery, the right of inspection, the effect of rejection, and the passage of title. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-ucc" secref="2-101 et seq." secrange="y">NYUCC &dblsect;2-101 et seq.</cite></para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alr5" titlename="Sales: construction and application of UCC sec. 2-612(2), dealing with rejection of goods under installment contracts" volref="61" pageref="611">Sales: construction and application of UCC sec. 2-612(2), dealing with rejection of goods under installment contracts, 61 A.L.R.5th 611</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alr5" titlename="What constitutes &ldquo;substantial impairment&rdquo; entitling buyer to revoke his acceptance of goods under UCC sec. 2-608(1)" volref="38" pageref="191">What constitutes &ldquo;substantial impairment&rdquo; entitling buyer to revoke his acceptance of goods under UCC sec. 2-608(1), 38 A.L.R.5th 191</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Sales and Exchanges of Personal Property" secref="73, 107, 108, 144 to 150" secrange="y">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Sales and Exchanges of Personal Property &dblsect;73, 107, 108, 144 to 150</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</item.reference>
<item.reference><name.block><label>Item</label><designator>8(a).</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|52|32:50"><para.text>The marketing agreement may fix specific sums as liquidated damages, which sums will not be regarded as penalties, payable for breach by a member or shareholder or contracting nonmember of the marketing obligation. A provision of this type may also be placed in the certificate of incorporation or bylaws. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="70" subref="(2)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;70(2)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="478">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;478</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="aj2" topicname="Cooperative Associations" secref="46">Am. Jur. 2d, Cooperative Associations &sect;46</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</item.reference>
<item.reference><name.block><label>Items</label><designator>8(b), (c).</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|52|32:50"><para.text>A corporation is given the right, in the event of a breach or threatened breach of a marketing contract by a member or by a contracting nonmember, to enjoin further breach of the contract and to obtain a decree of specific performance to enforce the contract. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-coopcorp" secref="70" subref="(3)">Coop. Corp. Law &sect;70(3)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alr4" titlename="Specific performance of sale of goods under UCC sec. 2-716" volref="26" pageref="294">Specific performance of sale of goods under UCC sec. 2-716, 26 A.L.R.4th 294</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="479">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;479</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="aj2" topicname="Cooperative Associations" secref="44">Am. Jur. 2d, Cooperative Associations &sect;44</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</item.reference>
<item.reference><name.block><label>Item</label><designator>9(a).</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|52|32:50"><para.text>The New York Uniform Commercial Code provides that in the case of sales, as in the case of contracts, generally, terms with respect to which the confirmatory memoranda of the parties agree or which are otherwise set forth in a writing intended by the parties as a final expression of their agreement with respect to such terms as are included therein may not be contradicted by evidence of any prior agreement or of a contemporaneous agreement. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-ucc" secref="2-202">NYUCC &sect;2-202</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alr4" titlename="Sales: construction of statute of frauds exception under UCC sec. 2-201(2) for confirmatory writing between merchants" volref="82" pageref="709">Sales: construction of statute of frauds exception under UCC sec. 2-201(2) for confirmatory writing between merchants, 82 A.L.R.4th 709</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Evidence and Witnesses" secref="558 to 620" secrange="y">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Evidence and Witnesses &dblsect;558 to 620</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Sales and Exchanges of Personal Property" secref="45">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Sales and Exchanges of Personal Property &sect;45</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</item.reference>
<item.reference><name.block><label>Item</label><designator>9(c).</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|52|32:50"><para.text>In general, rights under a contract involving no personal confidential relation and no exceptional personal skill or knowledge are assignable. An executory contract which is not personal in character and which can, consistent with the rights and interests of the adverse party, be sufficiently executed by the assignee, is assignable, in the absence of an agreement to the contrary. <cite type="case">Special Products Mfg., Inc. v. Douglass, 159 A.D.2d 847, 553 N.Y.S.2d 506 (3d Dep&apos;t 1990)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|52|32:50"><para.text>The courts will generally recognize and enforce a provision in a contract expressly prohibiting its assignment. <cite type="case">Sacks v. Neptune Meter Co., 144 Misc. 70, 258 N.Y.S. 254 (App. Term 1932), aff&apos;d, 238 A.D. 82, 263 N.Y.S. 462 (1st Dep&apos;t 1933)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Assignments" secref="7 to 14" secrange="y">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Assignments &dblsect;7 to 14</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</item.reference>

<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>32:51</designator><name>Marketing contract between cooperative and producer for purchase and sale of agricultural products</name></outline.name.block>

<section.body>
<form uuid="Ia39dc160181a11e68738d3db3a7c8dd3">
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><form.text>Agreement made on <inline.instr>&lsqb;date of agreement&rsqb;</inline.instr>, between <inline.instr>&lsqb;name of corporation&rsqb;</inline.instr>, a nonprofit cooperative corporation organized under the laws of the State of New York, referred to as &ldquo;Corporation,&rdquo; whose principal place of business and address for receiving correspondence regarding this agreement is <inline.instr>&lsqb;address of corporation&rsqb;</inline.instr>, <inline.instr>&lsqb;name of city&rsqb;</inline.instr>, <inline.instr>&lsqb;name of county&rsqb;</inline.instr>, <inline.instr>&lsqb;name of state&rsqb;</inline.instr>, and <inline.instr>&lsqb;name of producer&rsqb;</inline.instr>, of <inline.instr>&lsqb;address of producer&rsqb;</inline.instr>, <inline.instr>&lsqb;name of city&rsqb;</inline.instr>, <inline.instr>&lsqb;name of county&rsqb;</inline.instr>, <inline.instr>&lsqb;name of state&rsqb;</inline.instr>, <inline.instr>&lsqb;an independent producer/a member of the corporation&rsqb;</inline.instr>, referred to as &ldquo;Producer.&rdquo;</form.text></form.para>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><form.text>In consideration of the following mutual covenants, Corporation and Producer agree as follows:</form.text></form.para>
<form.unit>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>1</designator><name>AGRICULTURAL PRODUCTS PURCHASED AND SOLD</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><form.text>Corporation buys from Producer and Producer sells to Corporation all <inline.instr>&lsqb;specification of products&rsqb;</inline.instr>, referred to as &ldquo;products,&rdquo; produced by or for Producer or acquired by Producer as landlord or lessor, which products are <inline.instr>&lsqb;specification of required attributes of product&rsqb;</inline.instr>, except products that Producer reserves for personal use and not for sale. Producer agrees to deliver all such products at places directed by Corporation.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>2</designator><name>TITLE AND RISK OF LOSS</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><form.text>Corporation and Producer agree that title to all products subject to this agreement shall pass as soon as they have a potential existence. However, risk of loss shall be borne by Producer until delivery.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>3</designator><name>CENTRAL AGENCY OR SIMILAR ASSOCIATION</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><form.text>Corporation may exercise any powers conferred on it under this agreement through any central agency of which Corporation and any other similar organization are or may become members.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>4</designator><name>ADVANCES ON PRODUCTS</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><form.text>Corporation agrees to make such advances to Producer on products delivered under this agreement as in the discretion of its board of directors may be justified by marketing conditions.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>5</designator><name>MANNER OF DETERMINING PRICE; REVOLVING FUND; POOLS</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><form.text>Corporation agrees to sell, either in the natural or processed state, products delivered by Producer under this agreement, together with the products delivered by other Producers, and to pay over ratably the net amount received therefrom as payment in full to Producer after making deductions:</form.text></form.para>
<form.unit>
<form.item><name.block><designator>(a)</designator></name.block><form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><form.text>to cover advances, interest on advances, costs of picking, gathering, harvesting, receiving, assembling, transporting, handling, grading, packing, inspecting, processing, financing, advertising, storing, insuring, selling, and marketing such products and products derived therefrom;</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><name.block><designator>(b)</designator></name.block><form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><form.text>to cover organization, operating, and maintenance expenses;</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><name.block><designator>(c)</designator></name.block><form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><form.text>for capital in a central agency;</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><name.block><designator>(d)</designator></name.block><form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><form.text>to cover a revolving fund retained for the purpose of building up such an amount of capital as may be deemed necessary by its board of directors from time to time; and</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><name.block><designator>(e)</designator></name.block><form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><form.text>as needed for revolving such capital in the manner that may be provided in the Corporation&apos;s bylaws.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
</form.unit>
<form.para><form.text>The aggregate of such deductions shall not exceed <inline.instr>&lsqb;&lsqb;percentage of gross sales price&rsqb;&percnt; of the gross sales price of such products and products derived therefrom/&lsqb;number of cents&rsqb; cents per &lsqb;bushel/carton/&lsqb;specification of other unit&rsqb;&rsqb;&rsqb;</inline.instr>.</form.text></form.para>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><form.text>Corporation, within the discretion of its board of directors, is authorized to establish, from time to time, daily, weekly, monthly, or seasonal pools of the agricultural products marketed by it of the same variety, grade, and quality. All Producers having such products in a particular pool shall share ratably in the net amount received therefrom.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>6</designator><name>DELIVERY OF PRODUCTS</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><form.text>All products shall be delivered by Producer at the earliest reasonable time after harvesting at such places as Corporation may direct, and with such identification at Producer&apos;s expense as may be prescribed by the Corporation.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>7</designator><name>LOSSES</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><form.text>Any loss that Corporation may suffer on account of inferior or damaged condition of products at delivery shall be charged against Producer.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>8</designator><name>ASSOCIATION&apos;S POWER TO ENCUMBER PRODUCTS</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><form.text>Producer further agrees that Corporation or central marketing agency, individually or jointly, shall have the power to borrow money for any purpose of Corporation or central marketing agency on the security of the products delivered to Corporation, the products derived therefrom, or on any evidence of such products, byproducts, or cash accounts arising from their sale and to give a lien, either legal or equitable thereon, as the absolute owner. Producer also agrees that Corporation or central marketing agency may grade, pool, or commingle any part of such products or products derived therefrom with other products or products derived therefrom of like grade and variety and shall exercise all other rights of ownership without limitation.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>9</designator><name>LIQUIDATED DAMAGES FOR PRODUCER&apos;S BREACH OF AGREEMENT</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><form.text>Producer and Corporation agree that this agreement is one of a series dependent for its true value on the adherence of each and all of the contracting parties to all such agreements and that the cancellation of this agreement for the failure of Producer to comply with it shall not affect other similar agreements. Producer and Corporation also agree that the remedy at law for any breach of this agreement would be inadequate and that it would be impracticable and extremely difficult to determine the actual damage resulting to Corporation should Producer fail to deliver the covered products, regardless of the cost of such failure.</form.text></form.para>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><form.text>Producer agrees to pay to Corporation as liquidated damages for all products sold, delivered, or withheld by or for Producer&apos;s benefit, other than in accordance with the terms of this agreement, <inline.instr>&lsqb;&dollar;&lsqb;dollar amount of liquidated damages for all product&rsqb;/the sum of &dollar;&lsqb;dollar amount of liquidated damages payable&rsqb; per &lsqb;specification of unit&rsqb; on all products&rsqb;</inline.instr>.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>10</designator><name>COSTS AND EXPENSES OF LEGAL ACTION</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><form.text>If Corporation files an action by reason of a breach or threatened breach of this agreement, Producer shall pay all court costs, costs for bonds and otherwise, expenses of travel and all expenses arising out of or caused by the litigation, and reasonable attorney&apos;s fees expended or incurred by it in such proceedings, and all such costs and expenses shall be included in the judgment.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>11</designator><name>INTEGRATION OF CERTIFICATE AND BYLAWS INTO AGREEMENT</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><form.text>The articles of incorporation and the bylaws of corporation, now or hereafter in effect, and this agreement constitute the entire agreement between Corporation and Producer.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>12</designator><name>OTHER AGREEMENTS; PRODUCER&apos;S APPLICATION FOR CORPORATION MEMBERSHIP</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><form.text>Corporation may enter into agreements with other Producers differing in terms from those contained in this agreement but consistent with the bylaws of Corporation without invalidating this agreement, provided that Producer at Producer&apos;s request may sign a similar agreement as a substitute for this agreement. By signing this agreement, Producer, unless already a member, applies for membership in Corporation, and the signing of this agreement by Corporation will constitute an acceptance of such application.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>13</designator><name>STANDARDS AND INSPECTION</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><form.text>Corporation or the central agency shall establish or adopt standards for products and shall make rules and regulations governing the product&apos;s handling and shipping and shall provide inspectors or graders to grade the products. Producer agrees to be bound by such grading and to observe such rules and regulations. Association or the central agency shall provide for the inspection of all products delivered under this agreement and, if any such products are not in proper condition for sale, they shall be prepared for sale at Producer&apos;s expense.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>14</designator><name>TERMINATION AND RENEWAL OF AGREEMENT</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><form.text>After this agreement has been in effect <inline.instr>&lsqb;number of years&rsqb;</inline.instr> years from the date of its acceptance by Corporation, either party to the agreement may terminate it in any year on the last day of the anniversary month in which this agreement was so accepted by notifying the other party in writing of this intention, such notice to be given between the <inline.instr>&lsqb;ordinal number of day&rsqb;</inline.instr> and <inline.instr>&lsqb;ordinal number of day&rsqb;</inline.instr> day of the month immediately prior to the effective date of termination. If neither party terminates this agreement in any year, it is mutually agreed that such failure shall constitute conclusive evidence that the parties have renewed this agreement for another year.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>15</designator><name>PAYMENT OF LIENS ON PRODUCTS</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><form.text>If there is a lien on any of the products delivered under this agreement, Producer authorizes Corporation or central agency to pay the holder of such lien from the proceeds derived from the sale of such products before any payment is made to Producer under this agreement.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>16</designator><name>NO OTHER AGREEMENTS</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><form.text>The parties agree that there are no oral or other conditions, promises, covenants, representations, or inducements in addition to or at variance with any other terms of this agreement and that this agreement represents the voluntary and clear understandings of both parties fully and completely.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
</form.unit>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><form.text>Executed on <inline.instr>&lsqb;date of execution&rsqb;</inline.instr>, at <inline.instr>&lsqb;name of city&rsqb;</inline.instr>, New York.</form.text></form.para>

<note.block>
<note.group note.head="taxnotes">
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><para.text>A farmer&apos;s cooperative must limit the amount of business it does with nonmembers. It may market products or purchase supplies and equipment for nonmembers only if: (i) the value does not exceed the value of the products, supplies, and equipment of members; and (ii) the value of the purchases made for those who are neither members nor producers does not exceed 15&percnt; of total purchases. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="521" subref="(b)" pararef="(4)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;521(b)(4)</cite>. In addition, buying and selling for its own profit, such as selling by-products of purchases made for members to nonmembers, will disqualify a cooperative, even if sales are minimal.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><para.text>This explains the inclusion of a provision like that of Section 12 in the above agreement, which makes the contract itself an application for membership and an acceptance of that application.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><para.text>The revolving fund method of financing referred to in Section 5 is a hybrid type of security that has elements of both debt and equity. Because of the dual nature of the certificates of interest that are issued in this fund, they have sometimes been declared to be stock and other times indebtedness. See <cite type="secondary" normalpub="mertens" secref="34A:1 et seq." secrange="y">Mertens Law of Federal Income Taxation &dblsect;34A:1 et seq.</cite> for a more complete discussion of the taxation of cooperatives and their patrons.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|53|32:51"><para.text>For background information and drafting principles concerning marketing contracts, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="32:48 to 32:50" secrange="y">&dblsect;32:48 to 32:50</cite>.</para.text></para>
</note.group>

<section.body>
<form uuid="Ia39e3690181a11e68738d3db3a7c8dd3">
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>Agreement made <inline.instr>&lsqb;date of agreement&rsqb;</inline.instr>, between <inline.instr>&lsqb;name of packer&rsqb;</inline.instr>, of <inline.instr>&lsqb;address of packer&rsqb;</inline.instr>, <inline.instr>&lsqb;name of city&rsqb;</inline.instr>, <inline.instr>&lsqb;name of county&rsqb;</inline.instr>, State of New York, referred to as &ldquo;Packer,&rdquo; and <inline.instr>&lsqb;name of corporation&rsqb;</inline.instr>, a cooperative marketing corporation having its principal place of business at <inline.instr>&lsqb;address of corporation&rsqb;</inline.instr>, <inline.instr>&lsqb;name of city&rsqb;</inline.instr>, <inline.instr>&lsqb;name of county&rsqb;</inline.instr>, State of New York, referred to as &ldquo;Corporation.&rdquo;</form.text></form.para>
<form.line align="c">RECITALS</form.line>
<form.unit>
<form.item><name.block><designator>1</designator></name.block><form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>Corporation is a cooperative marketing corporation organized under the laws of the State of New York.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><name.block><designator>2</designator></name.block><form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>Corporation has secured crop contracts for numerous growers in the State of New York.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><name.block><designator>3</designator></name.block><form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>As a result of those contracts, Corporation will market a large proportion of the crop of <inline.instr>&lsqb;name of fruit&rsqb;</inline.instr>, referred to in this agreement as &ldquo;fruit,&rdquo; produced in the State of New York.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><name.block><designator>4</designator></name.block><form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>Packer is in the business of handling, processing, and packaging such fruit and desires to secure an adequate and certain supply of fruit for handling, processing, and packaging and to save the labor and expense of soliciting orders or contracts from the individual producers of such fruit.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><name.block><designator>5</designator></name.block><form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>Corporation is empowered to buy and sell the fruit of its members. In consideration of the above and the mutual promises of the parties to this contract, it is agreed as follows:</form.text></form.para></form.item>
</form.unit>
<form.unit>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>1</designator><name>SALE OF FRUIT</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>During the term of this contract, Corporation shall sell to Packer for handling, processing, and packaging in its plants, and Packer shall purchase and accept from Corporation for handling, processing, and packaging in its plants such fruit grown by members of the Corporation as follows:</form.text></form.para>
<form.unit>
<form.item><name.block><designator>A</designator></name.block><form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>All such fruit grown by certain members of the Corporation during the <inline.instr>&lsqb;identification of year&rsqb;</inline.instr> season as set forth and identified in Exhibit <inline.instr>&lsqb;designation of exhibit&rsqb;</inline.instr> attached and made a part of this contract.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><name.block><designator>B</designator></name.block><form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>All such fruit grown during the <inline.instr>&lsqb;identification of year&rsqb;</inline.instr> season by the members of the Corporation identified on Exhibit <inline.instr>&lsqb;designation of exhibit&rsqb;</inline.instr> attached and made a part of this contract, except to the extent that such Exhibit <inline.instr>&lsqb;designation of exhibit&rsqb;</inline.instr> may be amended by mutual agreement of Corporation and Packer.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
</form.unit></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>2</designator><name>TERM OF CONTRACT</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>This contract shall cover the crops of fruit grown during the <inline.instr>&lsqb;designation of season&rsqb;</inline.instr> season and the <inline.instr>&lsqb;designation of season&rsqb;</inline.instr> season.</form.text></form.para>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>&ldquo;Season,&rdquo; as used in this agreement, means that period commencing with the <inline.instr>&lsqb;ordinal number of day&rsqb;</inline.instr> day of <inline.instr>&lsqb;name of month&rsqb;</inline.instr> of one calendar year and ending with the <inline.instr>&lsqb;ordinal number of day&rsqb;</inline.instr> day of <inline.instr>&lsqb;name of month&rsqb;</inline.instr> of the following calendar year.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>3</designator><name>SEPARATE LISTING OF EACH GROWER</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>The ability of Corporation to deliver the fruit hereby sold to Packer is based and dependent on Corporation&apos;s crop contract with its grower&ndash;-members. If Corporation is unable to perform this contract because of any failure in performance of any of the provisions of the grower&ndash;-members&apos; contracts to Corporation or by clauses beyond Corporation&apos;s direct control, the mutual obligations and terms of this contract will not be affected, changed, or released as to any fruit from any other grower that is listed for the current crop year to Packer under this contract. For purposes of this section, each grower herein listed to packers shall be deemed listed to Packer under the terms of this contract separately from every other grower&ndash;-member listed to Packer under the terms of this contract, as though each grower&ndash;-member were covered by a separate contract with Packer.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>4</designator><name>INABILITY OF PACKER TO PERFORM</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>In case of fire, boiler explosion, interruption of power, strikes or other labor disturbances, lack of transportation facilities, shortage of labor supplies, perils to the city, floods, earthquakes, action of the elements, invasion, war, riot, insurrection, rebellion, interference of civil or military authorities, enactment of legislation, or any unavoidable casualty or cause beyond the Packer&apos;s control, affecting the conduct of Packer&apos;s business to the extent of preventing or unreasonably restricting, receiving, handling, processing, or packaging operations, including any obligation on Packer&apos;s part to transfer the fruit covered by this agreement or to furnish bins therefor, Packer will be excused for performance under this contract during the period that Packer&apos;s business or packaging operations are so affected. Packer may, during such period, accept such portion of the fruit as Packer has informed Corporation in its judgment it can economically handle.</form.text></form.para>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>Packer shall immediately give Corporation written notice of Packer&apos;s inability to perform and the specific cause or causes thereof. In any event, Packer shall pay, according to contract, for all fruit received by Packer.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>5</designator><name>DIVERSION TO OTHER PACKERS</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>With respect to the fruit that Packer has advised Corporation of its inability to handle pursuant to Section 4, Corporation retains the right, without liability of any kind or character to Packer, to divert the fruit to a Packer who is able to accept it in order to prevent economic waste to the growers and consumers.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>6</designator><name>FAILURE OF ASSOCIATION TO DELIVER</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>If, for the same causes enumerated in Section 4, the farming operations of any grower&ndash;-member of fruit covered by this agreement are so affected that such member or members are unable to make complete delivery of the fruit, Corporation shall make every reasonable effort to complete deliveries under this contract. However, Corporation shall be excused from the performance of that part of the contract that it is unable to perform because of these causes during the period the member&apos;s farming operations are so affected.</form.text></form.para>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>Corporation shall not be liable for the failure to deliver fruit destroyed by rain, frost, flood, or other similar casualties.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>7</designator><name>INDIVIDUAL AGREEMENTS WITH PACKER</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>Members of Corporation may enter into individual agreements with Packer with respect to delivery of fruit and advances for growing, harvesting, and other costs as indicated below. The form of the agreements between individual grower&ndash;-members of Corporation and Packer shall be in the form outlined in Exhibit <inline.instr>&lsqb;designation of exhibit&rsqb;</inline.instr> attached and made a part of this contract.</form.text></form.para>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>Packer shall furnish to each such grower&ndash;-member a copy of the agreement at the time of its execution.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>8</designator><name>PAYMENT OF EXPENSES</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>Packer shall pay expenses of delivering, weighing, inspecting, and receiving of all fruit subject to this agreement in accordance with its present customs and practices in the industry.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>9</designator><name>INSPECTION BY ASSOCIATION</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>Corporation shall have the right at any time by its authorized agents to examine and inspect any fruit held by Packer on account of Corporation under memorandum receipt or other similar arrangement.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>10</designator><name>SETTLEMENT STATEMENT</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>Packer shall furnish to each grower&ndash;-member of Corporation covered by this contract and to Corporation itself at the time of final settlement for fruit delivered under this contract for each crop year a copy of the settlement statement together with financial calculations indicating grower&apos;s returns.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>11</designator><name>FURNISHING OF BINS</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>Packer shall use its best efforts to furnish the grower&ndash;-members of Corporation bins in clean and good repair for the purpose of delivering fruit in accordance with its present customs and practices in the industry.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>12</designator><name>FAILURE TO SUPPLY BINS</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>If Packer shall neglect or fail to meet the reasonable bin requirements of grower&ndash;-members of Corporation covered by this agreement, Packer shall pay Corporation damages sustained by the grower&ndash;-members and Corporation on account of such neglect or failure.</form.text></form.para>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>Packer shall not be liable for damages when Packer cannot supply bins because of strikes, fire, acts of God, or other causes beyond Packer&apos;s control and of which notice has been given to Corporation under Section 4 of this contract. Packer shall not be liable for damages when Packer has allocated bins on a reasonable basis among grower&ndash;-members of Corporation and other growers from which Packer purchases fruit.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>13</designator><name>QUALITY AND GRADE OF FRUIT</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>All fruit delivered under this contract shall be of the quality and grades in effect for such fruit as may be developed and established by Packer or Corporation with approval of the other. In the event Packer establishes various grades by which different prices of grade may be paid grower&ndash;-members, Corporation may establish prices for its grower&ndash;-members on the basis of grade in accordance with the provisions of Sections 16 through 22.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>14</designator><name>COMPLIANCE WITH FAIR LABOR STANDARDS ACT</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>Corporation guarantees that all of the fruit subject to this contract was or will be produced and delivered in compliance with all applicable standards of the Fair Labor Standards Act (<cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="29" secref="201 et seq." secrange="y">29 U.S.C.A. &dblsect;201 et seq.</cite>), as amended.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>15</designator><name>BREACH OF GUARANTIES</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>Should Corporation breach any of the guaranties in Sections 13 or 14, Packer may, at its option, refuse to accept delivery. Packer shall have no obligation to pay for the crop, and Corporation may dispose of the crop free of the contract.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>16</designator><name>TONNAGE TO BE SOLD</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>Corporation shall sell to Packer and Packer shall purchase and accept from Corporation the following tonnage of such fruit: <inline.instr>&lsqb;number of tons of fruit&rsqb;</inline.instr> grown by members of Corporation covered by this contract at the price or prices indicated below.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>17</designator><name>FAILURE TO AGREE ON PRICE</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>If the parties to this agreement fail to agree on a price or prices under Sections 18 and 19 of this contract, Packer shall pay and Corporation shall accept for all fruit delivered to Packer by Corporation or the growers it represents a reasonable price, as that term is used in Section 18.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>18</designator><name>ASCERTAINMENT OF REASONABLE PRICE</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>The reasonable price referred to in Section 17 shall be ascertained in the following manner:</form.text></form.para>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>Corporation shall announce an opening price or prices that Corporation believes to be a reasonable price for each variety and grade or grades for any crop year on or before the <inline.instr>&lsqb;ordinal number of day&rsqb;</inline.instr> day of <inline.instr>&lsqb;name of month&rsqb;</inline.instr> of such year. Such announcement shall be made on the basis of consultations with individual packers and an examination by Corporation of all available economic and supply data that influence the sale and purchase price of such fruit.</form.text></form.para>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>Packer shall advise Corporation within <inline.instr>&lsqb;number of days&rsqb;</inline.instr> days after receipt of the announced opening price or prices for the <inline.instr>&lsqb;name of fruit&rsqb;</inline.instr> season of its acceptance or rejection of the price or prices. On the acceptance of the announced price or prices by <inline.instr>&lsqb;fraction of packers&rsqb;</inline.instr> in number of packers who purchase fruit from Corporation and those aggregate purchases represent <inline.instr>&lsqb;fraction of estimated total tonnage&rsqb;</inline.instr> of the estimated total tonnage of fruit offered for sale by Corporation under contracts of sale similar to this agreement, such opening price or prices shall be the reasonable price, provided, however, that among the requisite <inline.instr>&lsqb;fraction of packers&rsqb;</inline.instr> of packers who accept the announced price or prices, there shall be included one Packer whose estimated purchase of fruit tonnage under contract with the Corporation for the season shall be one of the <inline.instr>&lsqb;number of largest estimated tonnages&rsqb;</inline.instr> largest estimated tonnages under contract between Corporation and any purchaser for the season.</form.text></form.para>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>For purposes of the following calculation, Corporation for the <inline.instr>&lsqb;identification of year&rsqb;</inline.instr> season shall refer to the estimated tonnage set forth in Exhibit <inline.instr>&lsqb;designation of exhibit&rsqb;</inline.instr> attached to this contract and similar exhibits to similar agreements with other packers of such fruit. For the <inline.instr>&lsqb;identification of year&rsqb;</inline.instr> season, Corporation shall refer to the list and estimates furnished to Packer and to other packers for the season in accordance with Sections 1 and 2 of this contract and similar agreements.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>19</designator><name>NONACCEPTANCE OF OPENING PRICE</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>If the requisite packers do not signify their acceptance of the announced opening price or prices within <inline.instr>&lsqb;number of days&rsqb;</inline.instr> days after the announcement, Corporation will hold further consultations with the individual packers and reconsider the data above referred to on or before the <inline.instr>&lsqb;ordinal number of day&rsqb;</inline.instr> day of <inline.instr>&lsqb;name of month&rsqb;</inline.instr>, the Corporation will make a second announcement of price or prices that Corporation believes to be a reasonable price, which price or prices may be the same as or different from those previously announced. Such price or prices set forth in the second announcement will be the reasonable price, if such price or prices are accepted within <inline.instr>&lsqb;number of days&rsqb;</inline.instr> days after the second announcement by the requisite packers.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>20</designator><name>ARBITRATION TO ESTABLISH PRICE</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>If the requisite packers do not signify their acceptance of the price or prices announced by Corporation under Sections 18 and 19, those sections will be null and void and of no further effect. The price to be paid under this contract will then be determined by three arbitrators. The decision of the majority of the arbitrators will be binding on the parties to this contract and will be final and conclusive as to a reasonable price for the then-current crop year.</form.text></form.para>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>The arbitrators will be selected in the following manner: <inline.instr>&lsqb;specification of selection method&rsqb;</inline.instr>.</form.text></form.para>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>Within <inline.instr>&lsqb;number of days&rsqb;</inline.instr> days following the appointment of the arbitrators, the arbitrators will meet to conduct a hearing to determine what a reasonable price will be for the current crop year. Within <inline.instr>&lsqb;number of days&rsqb;</inline.instr> days of the close of such hearing, the arbitrators will report their decision, which, when signed by a majority of them, will be final and not subject to review.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>21</designator><name>DAMAGES FOR FAILURE TO RECEIVE FRUIT</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>If Packer, for any reason other than a price dispute, fails, neglects, or refuses, without just legal cause, to receive prior to the <inline.instr>&lsqb;ordinal number of day&rsqb;</inline.instr> day of <inline.instr>&lsqb;name of month&rsqb;</inline.instr> of any crop season covered by this agreement any fruit sold under this contract and that Packer is obligated by this agreement to receive, Packer will pay all reasonable damages caused by such failure unless the receiving date is extended by mutual agreement of grower-members, Packer, and Corporation.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>22</designator><name>PAYMENT FOR FRUIT</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>Unless otherwise agreed upon by grower and Packer, payments to grower-members of Corporation who deliver fruit under this agreement will be made by Packer within <inline.instr>&lsqb;number of days&rsqb;</inline.instr> days after full delivery and establishment of price and on demand for payment by grower-members.</form.text></form.para>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>The division of payments for fruit will be as follows: <inline.instr>&lsqb;percentage of payments due to grower-member&rsqb;</inline.instr>&percnt; of the payments due on delivered fruit shall be paid directly from Packer to grower-members, and <inline.instr>&lsqb;percentage of payments due to corporation&rsqb;</inline.instr>&percnt; of the payments due on delivered fruit and the entire service charge, as referred to in Section 25 of this contract, shall be paid to Corporation in accordance with the terms of that section.</form.text></form.para>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>If Packer, for any reason, fails to pay for the fruit or any other charges that Packer is obligated by this agreement to pay, either to grower&ndash;-members directly or to Corporation, on the date or dates agreed upon, interest at <inline.instr>&lsqb;percentage rate of monthly interest&rsqb;</inline.instr>&percnt; per month or any part of the month on the unpaid balance will commence to run immediately on such default.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>23</designator><name>DEFAULT BY PACKER</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>If Packer shall default or fail in the performance of any of its obligations under this contract, Corporation may stop any further deliveries to Packer and may deliver the balance of fruit elsewhere. This right may be exercised at any time although Corporation has permitted deliveries to Packer to continue after such default or failure. Continuance of delivery after Packer&apos;s default or failure in the performance of any of its obligations shall not be construed as a waiver of Corporation&apos;s right to stop deliveries. Such delivery of fruit elsewhere shall not be a waiver or release of any liability of Packer for default or failure in performance. Packer may be held liable to Corporation or its grower-members for damages suffered as a result of such default.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>24</designator><name>DEFAULT BY CORPORATION</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>If Corporation shall default or fail in the performance of any of its obligations under this contract, Packer may stop any further acceptance of fruit under the contract. This right may be exercised at any time although Packer has accepted delivery from Corporation members after such default or failure in the performance of any of its obligations under this contract. Continuance of delivery after Corporation&apos;s default or failure will not be construed as a waiver of Packer&apos;s right to stop receiving. Termination of receiving shall not be a waiver or release of any liability of Corporation for default or failure in performance. Corporation may also be held liable to Packer for damages suffered as a result of the default.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>25</designator><name>SERVICE CHARGE</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>Packer recognizes that the organization and continued existence of Corporation relieves Packer of the trouble, labor, and uncertainty of soliciting and obtaining separate contracts with individual growers for the purchase and sale of fruit. In consideration thereof, Packer shall pay to Corporation, over and above the market price designated in this agreement, a service charge of &dollar;<inline.instr>&lsqb;dollar amount of service charge&rsqb;</inline.instr> per ton for all fruit delivered to Packer under this contract and for all fruit delivered by agency growers who are members of Corporation. The service charge shall not be construed to be a part of the purchase price under this agreement.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>26</designator><name>SALE TO OTHER PACKER</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>If, during the terms of this agreement, Corporation sells to any Packer fruit of its grower-members at a price less than the price specified in Sections 16 through 21, Corporation will pay to Packer, on all fruit purchased under this contract, the difference between the price established in this agreement and the lowest price at which Corporation shall make sales to other packers.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>27</designator><name>DISAGREEMENT</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>In case any disagreement arises between the parties to this contract, either as to procedures under or interpretations of disagreement, there shall be an arbitration in the manner and under the conditions provided in Section 20.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>28</designator><name>PURCHASE AT DIFFERENT PRICE</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>If Packer, during or for any season under this contract, has purchased or has agreed to purchase any fruit from a grower-member of Corporation, from anyone other than Corporation, or from anyone other than a member of Corporation at a higher price or prices than established in this agreement in accordance with Sections 16 through 21, either upon the basis of grade or without grades, Packer will pay to Corporation for fruit purchased under this contract the highest price that Packer has paid or has agreed to pay or shall have paid or shall have agreed to pay for fruit so purchased from anyone.</form.text></form.para>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>In computing the higher purchase price so paid or agreed to be paid, there shall be included any bonuses, premiums, hauling or loading allowances, expenses of special services of any character that may be rendered by Packer or at its expense, and any sums paid or agreed to be paid by Packer for any other designated purpose than payment of purchase price. Nothing contained in this section shall apply to sales of fruit between packers.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
<form.item><head><name.block><designator>29</designator><name>SUPREMACY OF LAW</name></name.block></head>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>This contract will be deemed modified to the extent necessary to comply with state and federal laws and any order, regulation, or license pursuant thereto and marketing agreement or order under the authority of law.</form.text></form.para></form.item>
</form.unit>
<form.para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><form.text>In witness, the parties have executed this agreement at <inline.instr>&lsqb;place of execution&rsqb;</inline.instr> the day and year first above written.</form.text></form.para>

<item.reference.block>
<item.reference><name.block><label>Sections</label><designator>17 to 21.</designator></name.block>
<para ct.id="6d0bf250b92611ef8747b569df12a67d|54|32:52"><para.text>Under the New York Uniform Commercial Code, as under prior statutory and case law, the parties, if they so intend, can conclude a contract for sale even though the price is not settled. Where not settled by the agreement, the price to be paid is a reasonable price at the time for delivery, if: (a) nothing is said as to price; (b) the price is left to be agreed by the parties and they fail to agree; or (c) the price is to be fixed in terms of some agreed market or other standard as set or recorded by a third person or agency and it is not so set or recorded. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-ucc" secref="2-305">NYUCC &sect;2-305</cite>.</para.text></para>
